- In the following cases, an appeal cannot be brought against a decision of the General Division made in the exercise of its original or appellate civil jurisdiction:
a. Situation 1: It is expressly provided by written law that no appeal is allowed: A case where it is expressly provided by any written law that the decision of the General Division is final or that an appeal cannot be brought against the decision of the General Division;
b. Situation 2: The case falls within Fourth Schedule of SCJA: A case specified in the Fourth Schedule, subject to any exception specified in that Schedule

Example of Fourth Schedule of SCJA --> if issue falls within any of this, NO RIGHT TO APPEAL AT ALL
- No right to appeal against GDHC’s decisions on: 
* Judgement or Order by consent (Para 1(b))
* Order giving or refusing Further and Better Particulars (FBP) (Para 1(h))
* Order to allow amendment to pleading – Unless: (Para 1(i)) --> i.e. order allowing amendment to pleading cannot be appealed, but if these 2 conditions are fulfilled then can appeal
(i) Application for amendment was made after expiry of limitation period; AND 
(ii) Amendment was to correct name of a party, alter capacity in which a party sues or to add/substitute a new cause of action 
* Order refusing security for costs (Para 1(j))
* Order giving or refusing interrogatories (Para 1(k))

- No right to appeal against GDHC decisions if: (Para 3)
* Parties have agreed in writing that GDHC’s decision is final unless:
a. Party’s decision to enter agreement is affected by fraud or illegality; OR 
b. There was a fundamental breach of natural justice in the proceedings which resulted in the decision 

No right to appeal against GDHC decision on: 
Fourth Schedule of Supreme Court of Judicature Act 
Para 1 – Situations of no appeal against GDHC judgement/decision 
- No appeal can be brought against decision of GDHC where: 
b. Judgement or Order by consent: The judgment or order is made by consent of the parties;
h. Order on further and better particulars: GDHC Judge makes an order giving or refusing further and better particulars;
i. Order to allow amendment to pleading – Unless application for amendment was made after expiry of limitation period and amendment was to correct name of a party, alter capacity in which a party sues or to add/substitute a new cause of action: GDHC Judge makes an order giving permission to amend a pleading, except if:
(i) The application for such permission is made after the expiry of any relevant period of limitation current at the date of issue of the originating claim; and
(ii) The amendment is an amendment to correct the name of a party or to alter the capacity in which a party sues, or the effect of the amendment will be to add or substitute a new cause of action;
j. Order refusing security for costs: GDHC Judge makes an order refusing security for costs
k. Order giving or refusing interrogatories: GDHC Judge makes an order giving or refusing interrogatories.

Para 2 – Para 1 does not apply to certain family cases
- Para 1 does not apply to any decision, judgment or order of the Family Division of the High Court involving the exercise of the appellate civil jurisdiction mentioned in section 23 of the Family Justice Act 2014

Para 3 – Where parties agreed that GDHC’s decision is final 
(1) No appeal can be brought against decision of GDHC where parties have agreed in writing signed by or on behalf of each party that the decision is final unless party seeking to appeal proves that: 
a. The decision is affected by fraud or illegality; or
b. There was a fundamental breach of the rules of natural justice in the proceedings resulting in the decision.
(2) An agreement mentioned in Para 3(1):
a. May be made before or after the decision to which the agreement relates is made; and
b. May relate to part of a decision, in which case references in Para 3(1) to a decision are to be read as references to that part of the decision.

**Step 2: If party has a right to appeal, does party require Court’s permission to appeal? 
Does the party need court’s permission to appeal before filing a notice of appeal?

Court’s permission to appeal against GDHC decision is required in 3 situations 
S29A(1) of SCJA
- In the following cases, permission is required before an appeal may be brought against a decision of the General Division made in the exercise of its original or appellate civil jurisdiction: 
a. Situation 1: It is expressly provided by written law that appeal requires permission: A case where it is expressly provided by any written law that an appeal may be brought only with permission, or that no appeal may be brought except with permission;
b. Situation 2: Where amount in dispute is less than 250k (Amount claimed is below 250k then need Court’s permission) => Exception: But if Fifth Schedule exception applies then permission is not required (even if below 250k): Subject to any exception specified in the Fifth Schedule, where the amount in dispute, or the value of the subject matter, at the hearing before the General Division (excluding interest and costs) does not exceed $250,000 or such other sum as may be specified by an order made under subsection (3)
c. Situation 3: Where case falls within Paras 3, 4(1) and 5(1) of Fifth Schedule: Subject to any exception specified in the Fifth Schedule, a case specified in paragraphs 3, 4(1) and 5(1) of that Schedule.

Situation 2: Where amount in dispute is less than 250k => Exception: But if Fifth Schedule exception applies then permission is not required even if amount in dispute is less than 250k
Para 2(2) of Fifth Schedule 
- Despite section 29A(1)(b), permission is not required to appeal against the following decisions of the General Division:
a. Any decision of the General Division made in the exercise of its original jurisdiction under any written law which requires that case to be decided by the General Division in the exercise of its original jurisdiction;
b. Any decision of the Family Division of the High Court made in the exercise of its original jurisdiction.

Situation 3: Where case falls within Paras 3, 4(1) and 5(1) of Fifth Schedule
Para 3 of Fifth Schedule
- Permission is required to appeal against GDHC decision in any of the following cases: 
a. Order giving unconditional leave to defend: Where a Judge makes an order giving unconditional permission to defend any proceedings;
b. Order giving conditional leave to defend: Where a Judge makes an order giving permission to defend any proceedings on condition that the party defending those proceedings pays into court or gives security for the sum claimed, except if the appellant is that party;
c. Order setting aside default judgement unconditionally: Where a Judge makes an order setting aside unconditionally a default judgment, regardless of how the default judgment was obtained (including whether by reason of a breach of an order of court or otherwise);
d. Order setting aside default judgement conditionally: Where a Judge makes an order setting aside a default judgment on condition that the party against whom the judgment had been entered pays into court or gives security for the sum claimed, regardless of how the default judgment was obtained (including whether by reason of a breach of an order of court or otherwise), except if the appellant is that party;
e. Order refusing to strike out an action: Where a Judge makes an order refusing to strike out:
(i) Action from OC/OS: An action or a matter commenced by an originating claim or by any other originating process; or
(ii) Pleadings: A pleading or a part of a pleading;
f. Only issue relates to costs or fees: Where the only issue in the appeal relates to costs or fees for hearing dates;
g. Where a Judge sitting in chambers makes a decision in a summary way on an interpleader summons where the facts are not in dispute;
h. Order refusing leave to amend pleading unless: Where a Judge makes an order refusing permission to amend a pleading, except if —
(i) Amendment application made after certain time AND: The application for permission is made after the expiry of any relevant period of limitation current at the date of issue of the originating claim; and
(ii) Amendment has certain effect: The amendment is an amendment to correct the name of a party or to alter the capacity in which a party sues, or the effect of the amendment will be to add or substitute a new cause of action;
i. Order giving security for costs: Where a Judge makes an order giving security for costs;
j. Order giving or refusing discovery of documents: Where a Judge makes an order giving or refusing discovery or inspection of documents;
k. Order refusing stay of proceedings: Where a Judge makes an order refusing a stay of proceedings;
l. Orders made at the hearing of any interlocutory application - Where a Judge makes an order at the hearing of any interlocutory application other than an application for any of the following matters:
(i) Except application for summary judgement: For summary judgment;
(ii) Except application for setting aside of default judgement: To set aside a default judgment;
(iii) Except application for striking out: To strike out an action or a matter commenced by an originating claim or by any other originating process, a pleading or a part of a pleading; --> BECAUSE AFTER STRIKING OUT AN APPLICATION, IT TERMINATES THE RIGHT OF THE CLAIMANT, SO THE CLAIMANT SHOULD HAVE A RIGHT TO APPEAL!
(iv) Except application to dismiss action: To dismiss an action or a matter commenced by an originating claim or by any other originating process;
(v) Except further and better particulars: For further and better particulars;
(vi) Except application for permission to attend pleading: For permission to amend a pleading;
(vii) Except application for security for costs: For security for costs;
(viii) Except application for discovery of documents: For discovery or inspection of documents;
(ix) Except application to vary or serve interrogatories: For interrogatories to be varied or withdrawn, or for permission to serve interrogatories;
(x) Except application for stay of proceedings: For a stay of proceedings;
--> IF PRESENT ON THIS LIST, MEANS YOU CAN APPEAL WITHOUT PERMISSION FROM THE COURT!
m. Where a Judge at the hearing of an appeal under section 17, 29, 35 or 44 of the Protection from Online Falsehoods and Manipulation Act 2019 refuses to set aside the Part 3 Direction, Part 4 Direction, Declaration or Account Restriction Direction (as the case may be) against which the appeal was brought.

Telecom Credit Inc v Midas United Group Ltd [2019] 1 SLR 131 
- General philosophy on interlocutory applications under paragraph 3(l) of Fifth Schedule SCJA
a. A party’s ability to appeal an interlocutory matter depends on the importance of that matter to the substantive outcome of the case
b. Matters that are non-appealable: Matters that send the matter back along the ordinary route to trial where parties’ substantive rights will be decided
c. Matters that are appealable subject to leave: Matters that do not directly determine substantive outcome of the case but may nevertheless have some material impact on it 
d. Matters that are appealable without leave: Matters that determines parties’ rights 
- Definition of “orders” in Fifth Schedule: Interlocutory order i.e. an order that does not finally dispose of parties’ rights
- Definition of “interlocutory application” in Fifth Schedule: An application whose determination might or might not finally determine the parties’ rights
- Implication: If the order made at the hearing of interlocutory application determines parties’ rights then leave is not required. 
- If the order does not determines parties’ rights then leave to appeal will be required

Para 4(1) of Fifth Schedule
- The permission of the appellate court is required to appeal against a decision of the Family Division of the High Court involving the exercise of the appellate civil jurisdiction mentioned in section 23 of the Family Justice Act 2014.

Para 5 of Fifth Schedule
(1) Permission required to appeal against GDHC decision if: The permission of the appellate court is required to appeal against a decision of the General Division (including the Family Division of the High Court), where —
a. Parties agree in writing that GDHC decision is final: The parties have agreed in writing signed by or on behalf of each party that the decision is final; AND
b. Party seeking to appeal must allege decision is affected by fraud or illegality or there was a fundamental breach of natural justice in proceedings resulting in decision: The party seeking to appeal alleges that:
(i) The decision is affected by fraud or illegality; or
(ii) There was a fundamental breach of the rules of natural justice in the proceedings resulting in the decision.
(2) An agreement mentioned in sub-paragraph (1)
a. May be made before or after the decision to which the agreement relates is made; and
b. May relate to part of a decision, in which case references in sub-paragraph (1) to a decision are to be read as references to that part of the decision.

Note:
- Procedure to obtain permission to appeal depends on whether it is an Order 18 or Order 19 case 

Court’s permission to appeal against DC/MAC is required in 2 situations 
S21 of SCJA 
- An appeal lies to the GDHC from decision of a DC/MAC only with the permission of that DC/MAC or the GDHC in the following cases:
a. Amount in dispute does not exceed $60k: Any case where the amount in dispute, or the value of the subject matter, at the hearing before that District Court or Magistrate’s Court (excluding interest and costs) does not exceed $60,000 or such other amount as may be specified by an order made under subsection (3)
b. Any case specified in the Third Schedule
	
Orders made by DC/MAC that are appealable only with permission 
Third Schedule
- An appeal lies to the General Division from a decision of a District Court or Magistrate’s Court only with the permission of that District Court or Magistrate’s Court or the General Division in any of the following cases:
a. Where a District Court or Magistrate’s Court makes an order giving unconditional permission to defend any proceedings;
b. Where a District Court or Magistrate’s Court makes an order giving permission to defend any proceedings on condition that the party defending those proceedings pays into court or gives security for the sum claimed, except if the appellant is that party;
c. Where a District Court or Magistrate’s Court makes an order setting aside unconditionally a default judgment, regardless of how the default judgment was obtained (including whether by reason of a breach of an order of court or otherwise);
d. Where a District Court or Magistrate’s Court makes an order setting aside a default judgment on condition that the party against whom the judgment had been entered pays into court or gives security for the sum claimed, regardless of how the default judgment was obtained (including whether by reason of a breach of an order of court or otherwise), except if the appellant is that party.



**Step 3: Is it an Order 18 or Order 19 case? 

Order 18 Case Order 19 Case- Appeals on applications in actions (interlocutory matters such as document production, striking out etc.) 
- DJ/MAC decisions on OAs 
- Appeals from Summons within O18 appeals or O 19 appeals 
- Appeals on Registrar’s assessment of damages 

E.g. of applications in actions 
a. Application for security for costs
b. Provisional attachment order (to bank account)
c. Injunctions or search orders 
d. Substituted service
e. Service out of Singapore
f. Setting aside service of originating process
g. Judgement in default of notice of intention to contest or not 
h. Judgement in default of defence
i. Summary judgement 
j. Striking out of action or defence 
k. Stay of whole action 
l. Stay of enforcement of judgement
m. Enforcement order
n. Permission to appeal 
o. Etc. 
- Appeals on judgements after trial (hearing on merits of OC/OA)  
- Appeals from judgement of DJ/MAG in OCs
- Appeals from judgement of GDHC 
- Appeals from judgement of ADHC 

- Appeals on judgements given because one or more parties are absent 
- Appeals on MAG/DJ assessment of damages 
- Appeals on committal order for contempt of Court 
- Appeals on prerogative (JR) order 
- Appeals against Disciplinary Tribunal under Medical Registration Act

Note: 
- If your action starts from OA (different from application in action) 
a. Appeal from DC/MAC to GDHC is Order 18 
b. Appeal from GDHC to ADHC/CA is Order 19 assuming that judgement was given?
Appeals which are governed by Order 18 
O 18 r 1(1) of ROC
- Order 18 applies to: 
a. Every appeal from:
(i) A decision made on an application in an action;
(ii) A decision made on an appeal against a decision mentioned in sub?paragraph (i);
(iii) A decision made on an appeal against a decision mentioned in sub?paragraph (ii);
(iv) A decision made on an assessment of damages or the taking of accounts by the Registrar; or
(v) A decision of an appellate Court on an application by summons in an appeal under this Order or Order 19; and
b. An application to the appellate Court relating to an appeal to the appellate Court under this Order.

O 18 r 1(2) of ROC
- An application in an action:
a. Includes any application: 
(i) Taken out after the action is commenced; 
(ii) Made for any consequential or incidental matter after judgment is given in the trial of an originating claim or the hearing on the merits in an originating application; or
(iii) For the enforcement of the judgment or order; and
b. Excludes:
(i) Any application taken out or heard on the same day as the hearing on the merits of an originating claim or an originating application, or at any time after the commencement of such hearing until the giving of the judgment; and
(ii) Any matter under appeal which is within the scope of Order 19.

Appeals which are governed by Order 19 
O 19 r 1 of ROC 
a. An appeal against any judgment of a Magistrate’s Court or District Court given:
(i) In a trial, including a case where judgment is given or the action is dismissed at trial because one or more parties are absent;
(ii) After damages are assessed or accounts are taken by a District Judge; or
(iii) In an application for a committal order for contempt of court;
b. An appeal against any judgment of the General Division (except a judgment of the Registrar of the Supreme Court);
c. An appeal against any judgment of the Appellate Division
d. An appeal from any tribunal to the Appellate Division or the Court of Appeal pursuant to any written law;
e. An application to the appellate Court relating to an appeal mentioned in paragraph (a), (b), (c) or (d); and
f. An appeal against an order or decision of a Disciplinary Tribunal under the Medical Registration Act.

Definition of “judgement” (O 19 r 3 ROC):
“judgment” means a judgment given by the lower Court —
(a)	in a trial, and includes a case where judgment is given or the action is dismissed at trial because one or more parties are absent;
(b)	after damages are assessed or accounts are taken;
(c)	in an application for a committal order for contempt of court;
(d)	in an application for a prerogative order; or
(e)	in an appeal against a judgment described in paragraphs (a) to (d);


*Step 4: Which division of Order 18 or Order 19 applies? 
Order 18
- Division 2: Appeals from Registrar to DJ 
- Division 3: Appeals from DJ/MAJ to GDHC 
- Division 4: Appeals from Supreme Court Registrar to GDHC
- *Division 5: Appeals GDHC to ADHC/CA => State briefly whether appeal is to ADHC or CA => Ctrl f – Allocation of appeals between ADHC and CA

Order 19
- Division 2: Appeals from DJ/MAJ to GDHC
- *Division 3: Appeals from GDHC to ADHC/CA => State briefly whether appeal is to ADHC or CA => Ctrl f – Allocation of appeals between ADHC and CA
- Division 4: Appeals from Disciplinary Tribunal under Medical Registration Act 
*Step 5: Applicant must ensure that time for appealing has started to run
- Applicant can only file application for permission to appeal/Notice to appeal when time for appealing has started to run  

For Order 18 Appeals: Time for appealing starts when lower Court has determined all matters in the application including costs 
O 18 r 3(1) of ROC
- Subject to any written law and paragraph (2), unless the Court otherwise orders, the time for the filing of an appeal and for the filing of an application for permission to appeal does not start to run until after the lower Court has heard and determined all matters in an application, including costs.

Different circumstances where there are different time for appealing 
a. A direction that “costs are to be assessed” is a determination on costs
b. SAPT before Registrar with multiple matters: In a SAPT before a Registrar with multiple matters => Time for appeal begins when all matters have been determined 
c. SAPT with matters before Registrar and matters before Judge: In a SAPT with matters before a Registrar and matters before a Judge: 
(i) Time for appeal begins against Registrar’s decision begins when Registrar has determined all matters 
(ii) Time for appeal begins against Judge’s decision begins when the Judge has determined all matters (including any appeal against a decision of the Registrar) 
d. SAPT with multiple matters and Request made to Court to hear Further Arguments: In a SAPT with multiple matters and where a request is made for the Court to hear Further Arguments => Time for appeal begins only after the Court affirms, varies or set aside the decision after hearing Further Arguments or certifies that no Further Arguments are required

O 18 r 3(2) of ROC
- For the purposes of this Rule:
a. Direction that “costs are to be assessed” is a determination on costs: A direction by the lower Court that costs are to be assessed is to be regarded as a determination on the issue of costs;
b. For SAPT before Registrar – all matters (whether part of appeal or not) must be determined: Subject to sub?paragraph (c), in the case of a single application pending trial dealing with more than one matter, for the purposes of paragraph (1), time does not run until all matters have been heard and determined;
c. For SAPT before Registrar and Judge: In the case of a single application pending trial, where one or more matters dealt with in the single application pending trial are to be heard before the Registrar and one or more other matters are to be heard before the Judge:
(i) Time for appeal against Registrar starts when Registrar determines all matters (whether part of appeal or not): The time for filing of an appeal against a decision of the Registrar runs when the Registrar has heard and determined all the matters to be heard before the Registrar, although there are matters before the Judge that may not have been heard and determined yet; AND
(ii) Time for appeal against Judge starts when Judge determines all matters (whether part of appeal or not) including any appeals against Registrar: For the purposes of determining when the time starts to run for the filing of an appeal and for the filing of an application for permission to appeal against a decision on a matter heard before the Judge, the lower Court is treated as having heard and determined all matters in the single application pending trial when the Judge has heard and determined all the matters before the Judge, including any appeal against a decision of the Registrar on a matter before the Registrar; and
* Explanation – some matters appear before Registrar, some matters appear before the Judge. If appealing against Judge’s decision, must wait for all matters to be decided by Judge, including matters that he hears on appeal from the Registrar 
d. For SAPT – Time for Request for Further Arguments: For the purposes of sub?paragraphs (b) and (c), in the case of a single application pending trial dealing with more than one matter, where a request is made for the Court (not including the Registrar) to hear further arguments in respect of any decision on a matter, the time for the filing of an appeal and for the filing of an application for permission to appeal against the decisions on all matters does not begin to run until that Court:
(i) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(ii) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required.

For Order 19 Appeals: Time for appealing starts when lower Court has determined all matters in the application including costs 
O 19 r 4(1) of ROC
- Unless the Court otherwise orders, the time for the filing of an appeal and for the filing of an application for permission to appeal does not start to run until after the lower Court has heard and determined all matters in the trial, including costs.

Direction that “costs are to be assessed” is a determination on costs
O 19 r 4(2) of ROC
- For the purposes of this Rule, a direction by the lower Court that costs are to be assessed is to be regarded as a determination on the issue of costs.

Step 6A: Order 18: Appeal from State Courts Registrar to DJ  
Part 1: Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after Registrar’s decision 
O 18 r 15
- A party who intends to appeal to a District Judge against a decision of the Registrar of the State Courts must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Registrar’s decision.

Part 2: Appellant must wait for Registrar to confirm record of decision 
Registrar may either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision 
O 18 r 16(1)
- The Registrar may give a summary of the points he or she has decided without the need to issue written grounds of decision.

Registrar must issue certification within 14 days of Appellant filing Notice of Appeal   
O 18 r 16(2)
- Registrar must certify within 14 days after the filing of the notice of appeal: 
a. Certification that Registrar already issued written grounds OR: That he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision;
b. Certification that Registrar intends to issue written grounds OR: That he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision; or
c. Certification that official record of hearing is sufficient: That the certified transcript of the official record of the hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently,
and if he or she does not do so, it is presumed that no further written grounds of decision will be issued.

If Registrar intends to issue written grounds => Registrar must do so as soon as possible => If not issued within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal 
O 18 r 16(3)
- If Registrar intends to issue written grounds: If the Registrar certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she will issue written grounds of decision:
a. Registrar must do so as soon as practicable: He or she must endeavour to do so as soon as it is practicable; and
b. If Registrar does not issue within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal: If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the certification, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal.

Part 3: Appellant/Respondent files written submissions, bundle of authorities
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 16(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions on why the Registrar’s decision is to be upheld, set aside or varied 
- Appellant/Respondent must file bundle of authorities accompanying the written submissions 

No other documents may be filed => Unless Appellate Court allows 
O 18 r 16(7)
- No documents other than what has been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the appellate Court otherwise orders

Only one set of submissions for each party 
O 18 r 16(10)
- There must not be more than one set of submissions for each party or set of parties represented by the same firm of solicitors.

Instructions for written submissions 
a. Must include appropriate costs orders 
b. Must be subject to page limit 
O 18 r 16(6)
- Written submissions:
* Must include submissions on appropriate costs orders to be made in appeal 
* Must be subject to a page limit of 35 pages 
=> O 18 r 16(8): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) in special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 16(9): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 16(8)(b)

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
O 18 r 16(5)
- Appellant must file written submissions and bundle of authorities with the following timeline:
a. If r 16(2)(a) applies – within 14 days of Registrar’s certification: Where the Registrar certifies under paragraph (2)(a) that he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
b. If r 16(2)(b) applies – within 14 days of Registrar notifying that written grounds are ready for collection: Where the Registrar certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies that a copy of the written grounds of decision is ready for collection;
c. If r 16(2)(c) applies – within 14 days of Registrar’s certification Where the Registrar certifies under paragraph (2)(c) that the certified transcript of the official record of hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
d. If presumed no written grounds – within 28 days of filing and service of Form 35: Where it is presumed under paragraph (2) that no further written grounds of decision will be issued, within 28 days after the filing and service of the notice of appeal;
e. If r 16(3)(b) applies – within 28 days of Registrar notifying appeal to proceed: Where the appellant has applied in writing to proceed with the appeal under paragraph (3)(b), within 14 days after the Registrar notifies that the appeal is to proceed.

Step 6B: Order 18: Appeals from DJ/MAJ to GDHC 
Part 1A: If Court’s permission is required – Appellant must file and serve application for Court’s permission 
Appellant must file and serve application on DJ/MAJ and interested parties within 14 days after DJ/MAJ’s decision 
O 18 r 19(1)
- Where permission to appeal is required, a party must apply to the District Judge or Magistrate for such permission and serve the application on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the District Judge’s or Magistrate’s decision.

If DJ/MAJ rejects permission => Appellant must file and serve application on GDHC and interested parties within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s rejection  
O 18 r 19(2)
- Where the District Judge or Magistrate does not grant permission to appeal, the party may apply to the General Division for such permission and must serve the application on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the District Judge’s or Magistrate’s decision not to grant permission.

If approve permission => Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 
O 18 r 19(3)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 18 r 19(4)
- GDHC can extend at any time: GDHC can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made at any time 
- DJ/MAJ can extend before time expires: DJ/MAJ can extend for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 1B: If Court’s permission is not required – Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s decision (another timeline if Request for Further Arguments made) 
O 18 r 17(1) 
- A party who intends to appeal to the General Division against the decision of a District Judge or Magistrate hearing any application at first instance, or against the decision of a District Judge hearing any appeal, must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35:
a. Within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s decision OR: Within 14 days after the date of the District Judge’s or Magistrate’s decision; or
b. If Request for Further Arguments has been made: In a case where a request for further arguments has been made under Rule 18, within 14 days after:
(i) Within 14 days after DJ/MAJ hears and decides Further Arguments: the District Judge or Magistrate affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; OR 
(ii) Within 14 days after DJ/MAJ decides Further Arguments not required: the parties are informed, or it is deemed, that the District Judge or Magistrate does not require further arguments.

Time extension for filing and service of Notice of Appeal  
O 18 r 17(2)
- GDHC can extend at any time: GDHC can extend time for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made at any time 
- DJ/MAJ can extend before time expires: DJ/MAJ can extend for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 2: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 18 r 20(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 18 r 20(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 20(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the following amounts:
a. $3,000 for an appeal against a decision in a Magistrate’s Court action;
b. $5,000 for an appeal against a decision in a District Court action.

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 18 r 20(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 18 r 20(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 3: Appellant must wait for DJ/MAJ to confirm record of decision 
 DJ/MAJ may either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision
O 18 r 21(1)
- The DJ/MAJ may give a summary of the points he or she has decided without the need to issue written grounds of decision.

DJ/MAJ must issue certification within 14 days of Appellant filing Notice of Appeal   
O 18 r 21(2)
- The DJ/MAJ must certify within 14 days after the filing of the notice of appeal: 
a. Certification that DJ/MAJ already issued written grounds: That he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision;
b. Certification that DJ/MAJ intends to issue written grounds: That he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision; or
c. Certification that Official record of hearing is sufficient: That the certified transcript of the official record of the hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently,
and if he or she does not do so, it is presumed that no further written grounds of decision will be issued.

If DJ/MAJ intends to issue written grounds => DJ/MAJ must do so as soon as possible => If not issued within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal 
O 18 r 16(3)
- If DJ/MAJ intends to issue written grounds: If the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she will issue written grounds of decision:
a. DJ/MAJ must do so as soon as practicable: He or she must endeavour to do so as soon as it is practicable; and
b. If DJ/MAJ does not issue within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal: If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the certification, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal.

Part 4: Appellant/Respondent files written submissions, bundle of authorities
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 21(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions on why the DJ/MAJ’s decision is to be upheld, set aside or varied 
- Appellant/Respondent must file bundle of authorities accompanying the written submissions 

No other documents may be filed => Unless Appellate Court allows 
O 18 r 21(11)
- No documents other than what has been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the appellate Court otherwise orders

Instructions for written submissions 
a. Must include appropriate costs orders 
b. Must be subject to page limit 
O 18 r 21(6)
- Written submissions:
* Must include submissions on appropriate costs orders to be made in appeal 
* Must be subject to a page limit of 35 pages 
=> O 18 r 21(16): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) in special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 21(17): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 21(16)(b)

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
O 18 r 16(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions and bundle of authorities with the following timeline:
a. If r 21(2)(a) applies – within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s certification: Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(a) that he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
b. If r 21(2)(b) applies – within 14 days of DJ/MAJ notifying that written grounds are ready for collection: Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies that a copy of the written grounds of decision is ready for collection;
c. If r 21(2)(c) applies – within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s certification Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(c) that the certified transcript of the official record of hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the DJ/MAJ;
d. If presumed no written grounds – within 28 days of filing and service of Form 35: Where it is presumed under paragraph (2) that no further written grounds of decision will be issued, within 28 days after the filing and service of the notice of appeal;
e. If r 21(3)(b) applies – within 28 days of DJ/MAJ notifying appeal to proceed: Where the appellant has applied in writing to proceed with the appeal under paragraph (3)(b), within 14 days after the Registrar notifies that the appeal is to proceed.

Step 6C: Order 18: Appeals from Supreme Court Registrar to GDHC
Part 1: If Court’s permission is not required – Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days of SC Registrar’s decision 
O 18 r 24 
- A party who intends to appeal to a Judge in Chambers against the decision of the Registrar of the Supreme Court must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Supreme Court Registrar’s decision 

Part 2: Appellant must wait for SC Registrar to confirm record of decision 
SC Registrar may either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision
O 18 r 25(1)
- The Registrar may give a summary of the points he or she has decided without the need to issue written grounds of decision.

SC Registrar must issue certification within 14 days of Appellant filing Notice of Appeal   
O 18 r 25(2)
- The DJ/MAJ must certify within 14 days after the filing of the notice of appeal: 
a. Certification that SC Registrar has already issued written grounds: That he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision;
b. Certification that SC Registrar intends to issue written grounds: That he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision; or
c. Certification that official record of hearing is sufficient: That the certified transcript of the official record of the hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently,
and if he or she does not do so, it is presumed that no further written grounds of decision will be issued.

If SC Registrar intends to issue written grounds => SC Registrar must do so as soon as possible => If not issued within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal
O 18 r 25(3)
- If SC Registrar intends to issue written grounds: If the SC Registrar certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she will issue written grounds of decision:
a. SC Registrar must do so as soon as practicable: He or she must endeavour to do so as soon as it is practicable; and
b. If SC Registrar does not issue within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal: If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the certification, the Appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal.

Part 3: Appellant/Respondent files written submissions, bundle of authorities
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 25(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions on why the SC Registrar’s decision is to be upheld, set aside or varied 
- Appellant/Respondent must file bundle of authorities accompanying the written submissions 

No other documents may be filed => Unless Appellate Court allows 
O 18 r 25(7)
- No documents other than what has been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the appellate Court otherwise orders

Instructions for written submissions 
a. Must include appropriate costs orders 
b. Must be subject to page limit 
O 18 r 25(6)
- Written submissions:
* Must include submissions on appropriate costs orders to be made in appeal 
* Must be subject to a page limit of 35 pages 
=> O 18 r 25(8): GDHC may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 21(9): GDHC may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 25(8)(b)

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities  
O 18 r 25(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities with the following timeline:
a. If r 25(2)(a) applies – within 14 days of SC Registrar’s certification: Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(a) that he or she has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
b. If r 25(2)(b) applies – within 14 days of SC Registrar notifying that written grounds are ready for collection: Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that he or she intends to issue written grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies that a copy of the written grounds of decision is ready for collection;
c. If r 25(2)(c) applies – within 14 days of SC Registrar’s certification Where the DJ/MAJ certifies under paragraph (2)(c) that the certified transcript of the official record of hearing sets out his or her grounds of decision sufficiently, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the DJ/MAJ;
d. If presumed no written grounds – within 28 days of filing and service of Form 35: Where it is presumed under paragraph (2) that no further written grounds of decision will be issued, within 28 days after the filing and service of the notice of appeal;
e. If r 25(3)(b) applies – within 14 days of Registrar notifying appeal to proceed: Where the appellant has applied in writing to proceed with the appeal under paragraph (3)(b), within 14 days after the Registrar notifies that the appeal is to proceed.

*Order 18 Div 5: Appeals from GDHC to ADHC/CA, Appeals from ADHC to CA 

*Part 1A: If Court’s permission is required – Appellant must file and serve application for appellate Court’s permission 
Scope of Order 18 Div 5 (O 18 r 26)
- Appeal to the AD/CA against any decision of the GDHC in relation to an application in an action (i.e. appeals made against decisions made in interlocutory matters)
- Appeal to CA against any decision of the ADHC in an application in an action
- Appeal to CA against any decision of the ADHC in relation to a summons in an appeal filed to the ADHC
- Applications to the AD/CA in relation to the appeals referred to above

O 18 r 1(2) of ROC
- An application in an action:
a. Includes any application: 
(iv) Taken out after the action is commenced; 
(v) Made for any consequential or incidental matter after judgment is given in the trial of an originating claim or the hearing on the merits in an originating application; or
(vi) For the enforcement of the judgment or order; and
b. Excludes:
(iii) Any application taken out or heard on the same day as the hearing on the merits of an originating claim or an originating application, or at any time after the commencement of such hearing until the giving of the judgment; and
(iv) Any matter under appeal which is within the scope of Order 19.
NB: No need to know procedure for seeking permission to appeal

Procedure is found in O 18 r 29 + O 18 r 35Step 1: Appellant must file and serve application (by OA or in summons if there is an existing appeal pending) on Appellate Court and interested parties within 14 days after Lower Court’s decision 
O 18 r 29(1)
- Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, a party must apply for such permission from appellate Court and file and serve the application and documents on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the lower Court’s decision

Appellant’s application for permission by OA or in summons (if appeal is pending before Appellate court)
O 18 r 35(1)
- Every application to the appellate Court must be made either by originating application or, in an appeal which is pending before the appellate Court, by summons
=> Applicant can file and serve an affidavit in support of the application 

Documents to be filed in Appellant’s application for permission
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 18 r 29(7)
- Appellant for permission under this Rule:
a. Must, at the time of filing the application, file written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
b. May, at the time of filing the application, file a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits

Prohibition on filing affidavits for application for permission to appeal
O 18 r 29(15)
- No affidavit is to be filed without permission of the appellate court 

Documents must be served on all interested parties 
O 18 r 29(9)
- The application, written submissions, any accompanying bundles of authorities and bundles of documents must be served on all parties who have an interest in the appeal

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 18 r 29(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 18 r 29(11))
=> O 18 r 29(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 29(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 29(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(1) Written submission in an application to appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(3) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD
Optional – Alters time to file and serve application for permission: Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before (1) Time of extraction of judgement, (2) 15th day after decision, or (3) Filing of application for Court’s permission to appeal (to appellate court)
O 18 r 29(2)
- Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before: Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, the Judge who made the decision may hear further arguments in respect of the decision if any party to the hearing, or the Judge, requests for further arguments pursuant to section 29B of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act before the earliest of the following:
a. Time which judgement is extracted: The time at which the judgment or order relating to the decision is extracted;
b. 15th day after decision: The 15th day after the date on which the decision is made;
c. Filing of application for permission: The time at which an application for permission to appeal against the decision is filed.

If request for Further Arguments made => Appellant can only file and serve application for permission to appeal within 14 days after Lower Court affirms/varies/sets aside decision after hearing Further Arguments or certifies that no Further Arguments are required
O 18 r 29(3)
- If a request for further arguments in respect of a decision has been made under paragraph (2):
a. An application for permission to appeal against the decision may not be filed against the decision until the lower Court:
(i) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(ii) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required; and
b. The party seeking to apply for permission to appeal must file and serve the application for permission to appeal against the decision, and the documents mentioned in paragraph (7), within 14 days after the date the lower Court:
(i) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(ii) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required.
Step 2: Appellant must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Appellant files the application 
O 18 r 35(5)
- The party who files an originating application or a summons to the appellate Court must provide security for the opposing party’s costs of the application and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time that party files the application
Form of Security 
O 18 r 35(8)
- Security must be
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent OR 
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; OR 
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 35(9)
- Applicant must provide security in the amount of $5,000 
Step 3: Respondent must file and serve affidavit in reply on Appellant and other parties within 14 days after Appellant serves OA and affidavit on Respondent
O 18 r 35(4)
- If the opposing party wishes, opposing party must file and serve an affidavit in reply on the applicant and other parties within 14 days after the date of application and affidavit is served on the respondent 

Documents to be filed by Respondent opposing application for permission 
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 18 r 29(8) 
- A party who wishes to oppose an application for permission under this Rule:
a. Must file and serve written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
b. May, together with the written submissions mentioned in sub?paragraph (a), file and serve a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits,

Instructions for Documents (same as application for permission to appeal, see above)

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents 
Respondent must file and serve within 14 days after Appellant’s application is made
O 18 r 29(8)
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 14 days after the application for permission is made by the Appellant
Step 4: Appellant/Respondent file written submissions and bundle of authorities to the appellate Court within 14 days after Respondent’s affidavit in reply is filed and served 

Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.

Instructions for Documents 
Must be subject to page limits 
O 18 r 37(2)
- Written submissions are subject to page limit of 35 pages
=> O 18 r 37(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 37(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 37(3)(b)

Contents of Written submissions 
O 18 r 37(6)
- The concluding paragraphs of the written submissions must include:
a. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made in the application; and
b. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the application.
Step 5: If Appellant gets permission to appeal, Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 

O 18 r 29(17)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 18 r 29(18)
- Appellate Court can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made at any time 

Other rules 
- O 18 r 29(16): No oral arguments are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders 
- O 18 r 29(15): No affidavit are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders

*Part 1B: If Court’s permission is not required (or after permission to appeal is granted) – Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days of Lower Court’s decision (another timeline if Request for Further Arguments made) 
O 18 r 27(1) 
- File and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties: A party who intends to appeal to the Appellate Court against the decision of a lower Court hearing any application or any appeal must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35:
a. Within 14 days of lower Court’s decision; OR
b. If Request for Further Arguments has been made – Within 14 days after date in s29B(4)(b) of SCJA: In a case where a request for further arguments has been made under s29B(2) of the SCJA, within 14 days after the date mentioned in s29B(4)(b) of SCJA 

Time extension for filing and service of Notice of Appeal  
O 18 r 27(2)
- Appellate Court can extend at any time: Appellate Court can extend time for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made at any time 
- Lower Court can extend before time expires: Lower Court can extend for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 2: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 18 r 30(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 18 r 30(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 30(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the amount of $15,000

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 18 r 30(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 18 r 30(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 3: Appellant must wait for Lower Court to confirm record of decision 
Lower Court may either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision 
O 18 r 33(1)
- The Lower Court may give a summary of the points he or she has decided without the need to issue written grounds of decision.

Lower Court must issue certification within 14 days of Appellant filing Notice of Appeal   
O 18 r 33(2)
- The Lower Court must certify within 14 days after the filing of the notice of appeal: 
a. Certification that lower Court already issued written grounds: That Lower Court has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision;
b. Certification that lower Court intends to issue written grounds: That Lower Court intends to issue written grounds of decision; or
c. Certification that Official record of hearing is sufficient: That the certified transcript of the official record of the hearing sets out Lower Court grounds of decision sufficiently,
and if Lower Court does not do so, it is presumed that no further written grounds of decision will be issued.

If Lower Court intends to issue written grounds => Lower Court must do so as soon as possible => If not issued within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal
O 18 r 33(3)
- If Lower Court intends to issue written grounds: If the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that it will issue written grounds of decision:
a. Lower Court must do so as soon as practicable: Lower Court must endeavour to do so as soon as it is practicable; and
b. If Lower Court does not issue within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal: If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the certification, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal.

Part 4: Appellant/Respondent files written submissions, bundle of authorities
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 33(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions on why the Lower Court’s decision is to be upheld, set aside or varied 
- Appellant/Respondent must file bundle of authorities accompanying the written submissions 

No other documents may be filed => Unless Appellate Court allows 
O 18 r 33(11)
- No documents other than what has been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the appellate Court otherwise orders

Instructions for written submissions 
a. Must include appropriate costs orders 
b. Must be subject to page limit 
O 18 r 33(6)
- Written submissions:
* Must include submissions on appropriate costs orders to be made in appeal 
* Must be subject to a page limit of 35 pages 
=> O 18 r 33(16): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 33(17): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 33(16)(b)
Formatting requirements for written submissions 
Para 120 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 
- Formatting requirements: 
a. The cover page(s), which are mandatory, must be included at the beginning of the document;
b. If a table of contents is mandatory under paragraph 119(4) of these Practice Directions, the table of contents must be included at the beginning of the document immediately after the cover page(s);
c. All pages must be paginated, with the page numbers corresponding to the Portable Document Format (PDF) version of the document;
d. The minimum font size to be used is Times New Roman 12 or its equivalent;
e. The print of every page must be double-spaced; and
f. Every page must have a margin on all 4 sides, each of at least 35 mm in width.

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
O 18 r 33(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions and bundle of authorities with the following timeline:
a. If r 33(2)(a) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court’s certification: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(a) that it has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
b. If r 33(2)(b) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court notifying that written grounds are ready for collection: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that it intends to issue written grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies that a copy of the written grounds of decision is ready for collection;
c. If r 33(2)(c) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court’s certification: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(c) that the certified transcript of the official record of hearing sets out its grounds of decision sufficiently, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Lower Court;
d. If presumed no written grounds – within 28 days of filing and service of Form 35: Where it is presumed under paragraph (2) that no further written grounds of decision will be issued, within 28 days after the filing and service of the notice of appeal;
e. If r 33(3)(b) applies – within 14 days of Registrar notifying appeal to proceed: Where the appellant has applied in writing to proceed with the appeal under paragraph (3)(b), within 14 days after the Registrar notifies that the appeal is to proceed.

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 18 r 33(12)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the written submissions within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 18 r 33(15)
- Where the respondent to the appeal fails to file and serve the written submissions for the appeal within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Step 6E: Order 19: Appeals from DJ/MAJ to GDHC
Part 1A: If Court’s permission is required – Appellant must file and serve application for Court’s permission 
Appellant must file and serve application on DJ/MAJ and interested parties within 14 days after DJ/MAJ’s judgement 
O 19 r 15(1)
- Where permission to appeal is required, a party must apply to the DJ/MAJ for such permission and serve the application on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the DJ/MAJ’s judgement

If DJ/MAJ rejects permission => Appellant must file and serve application on GDHC and interested parties within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s rejection  
O 19 r 15(2)
- Where the DJ/MAJ does not grant permission to appeal, the party may apply to the GDHC for such permission and must serve the application on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the DJ/MAJ’s decision not to grant permission.

If approve permission => Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 
O 19 r 15(3)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 19 r 15(4)
- GDHC can extend at any time: GDHC can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made at any time 
- DJ/MAJ can extend before time expires: DJ/MAJ can extend for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 1B: If Court’s permission is not required – Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days of DJ/MAJ’s judgement (another timeline if Request for Further Arguments made) 
O 19 r 14(1) 
- A party who intends to appeal to the GDHC against the judgement of a DJ/MAJ must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the DJ/MAJ’s judgement

Time extension for filing and service of Notice of Appeal  
O 19 r 14(2)
- GDHC can extend at any time: GDHC can extend time for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made at any time 
- DJ/MAJ can extend before time expires: DJ/MAJ can extend for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 2: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 19 r 16(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 19 r 16(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 19 r 16(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the following amounts:
a. $3,000 for an appeal against a decision in a Magistrate’s Court action;
b. $5,000 for an appeal against a decision in a District Court action.

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 18 r 16(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 18 r 16(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 3: Appellant must wait for DJ/MAJ to confirm record of decision 
DJ/MAJ must give written grounds of decision after Appellant files Notice of Appeal  
O 19 r 17(1)
- DJ/MAJ must issue its written grounds of decision after the notice of appeal has been filed if DJ/MAJ has not already done so 

Registry will notify parties when record of proceedings ready for collection
O 19 r 17(2)
- The Registry must notify the parties when the record of proceedings is ready for collection.

If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks of filing Notice of Appeal => Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal and for a copy of record of proceedings 
O 19 r 17(3)
- If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the date of filing of the notice of appeal, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal and for a copy of the record of proceedings.

Part 4: Appellant files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Record of Appeal, (2) Appellant’s Case, (3) Appellant’s core bundle of documents, (4) Appellant’s bundle of authorities
O 19 r 17(4)
- Appellant must file and serve: 
a. Record of appeal 
b. Appellant’s Case
c. Appellant’s core bundle of documents, with the written judgement or grounds of decision of the DJ/MAJ and the extracted order of the DJ/MAJ in a separate volume 
d. Appellant’s bundle of authorities 

Instructions for Appellant’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Appellant’s Case – 35 pages (O 19 r 19(1)(a))
- Appellant’s core bundle of documents (excluding the written judgment or grounds of decision of the lower Court and the extracted order of the lower Court) — 55 pages (O 19 r 19(2)(a))
=> O 19 r 19(3): GDHC may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 19(4): GDHC may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 19(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Case 
O 19 r 18(1)
- Appellant’s Case must contain the following: 
a. Succinct summary of the facts, the decision of the lower Court, contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the General Division;
b. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the lower Court;
c. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal and the appellant’s core bundle of documents;
d. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal;
e. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
f. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor.

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve documents
Within 28 days after Registry informs parties that record of proceedings available 
O 19 r 17(4)
- Appellant must file and serve documents within 28 days after the date on which the Registry informs the parties that the record of proceedings is available

Part 5: Respondent files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Respondent must file (1) Respondent’s Case, (2) Respondent’s core bundle of documents, (3) Respondent’s bundle of authorities
O 19 r 17(8)
- Respondent must file and serve: 
a. Respondent’s Case
b. Respondent’s core bundle of documents (if necessary) 
c. Respondent’s bundle of authorities

Instructions for Respondent’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Respondent’s Case – 35 pages (O 19 r 19(1)(b))
- Respondent’s core bundle of documents — 35 pages (O 19 r 19(2)(b))
=> O 19 r 19(3): GDHC may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 19(4): GDHC may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 19(3)(b)

Contents of Respondent’s Case 
O 19 r 18(2)
- Respondent’s Case must contain the following: 
a. A succinct summary of the contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the General Division;
b. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the lower Court;
c. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal and the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any);
d. If the respondent intends to submit that:
(i) The lower Court’s decision should be varied should the appeal be wholly or partially allowed where the respondent has not appealed against the decision of the lower Court; or
(ii) The lower Court’s decision should be affirmed on grounds other than those relied upon by that Court,
the respondent must state so in the respondent’s Case and set out the reasons for the respondent’s submissions;
e. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal;
f. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
g. The name and signature of the respondent’s solicitor.

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents
Within 28 days after Appellant serving documents
O 19 r 17(8) 
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 28 days after Appellant serves documents mentioned in r 17(4)

Part 6: Appellant files and serves Reply
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Appellant’s Reply, (2) Second Core Bundle and (2) Appellant’s Bundle of Authorities 
O 19 r 17(10)
- Appellant must file and serve:
a. Appellant’s Reply (if any)
b. Second core bundle (if necessary)
c. Appellant’s second bundle of authorities (if any) 

Instructions for Appellant’s Reply
a. Must be subject to page limit 
- Appellant’s Reply – 20 pages (O 19 r 19(1)(c))
- Appellant’s second core bundle — 25 pages (O 19 r 19(2)(c))
=> O 19 r 19(3): GDHC may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 19(4): GDHC may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 19(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Reply 
O 19 r 18(4)
- Appellant’s Reply must contain the following: 
a. The appellant’s detailed submissions in reply to the respondent’s submissions;
b. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the appellant’s core bundle of documents, the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any), and the second core bundle (if any);
c. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor.

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve Reply 
Within 14 days of Respondent serving documents
O 19 r 17(10) 
- Appellant must file and serve Reply within 14 days after the Respondent’s Case is served on the Appellant

Other instructions on documents 
Appellant’s Case, Respondent’s Case and Appellant’s Reply must be self-contained
O 19 r 18(5)
- The appellant’s Case, the respondent’s Case and the appellant’s Reply must contain everything that the parties intend to put forward at the appeal and must be prepared on the basis that there will be no need to supplement or to elaborate on any points made.

No other documents allowed
O 19 r 19(19)
- No documents other than what have been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the General Division otherwise orders.

*Order 19 Div 3: Appeals from GDHC to ADHC/CA, Appeals from ADHC to CA

*Part 1A: If Court’s permission is required – Appellant must file and serve application for appellate Court’s permission 
Scope of Order 19 Div 3 (O 19 r 24)
- Appeal to the AD/CA against a judgement of the GDHC
- Appeal to the CA against a judgement of the ADHC
- Applications to the AD/CA in relation to the appeals referred to above
- Appeals from tribunals pursuant to written law

Cover appeal against decisions made after the substantive hearing or trial of an OA (after full blown hearing) or OC (after full blown trial).

Definition of “Judgement” (O 19 r 3)
- Means a judgement given by the lower Court – 
(a) in a trial, and includes a case where judgment is given or the action is dismissed at trial because one or more parties are absent;
(b) after damages are assessed or accounts are taken;
(c) in an application for a committal order for contempt of court;
(d) in an application for a prerogative order; or
(e) in an appeal against a judgment described in paragraphs (a) to (d);

Definition of “trial” (O 19 r 3)
- Means the hearing on the merits of an originating claim or an originating application and includes all applications taken out or heard on the same day as such hearing and at any time after the commencement of such hearing until the giving of the judgment

NB: No need to know procedure for seeking permission to appeal

Procedure is found in O 19 r 26 + O 19 r 35Step 1: Appellant must file and serve application (by OA or in summons if there is an existing appeal pending) on Appellate Court and interested parties within 14 days after Lower Court’s decision 
O 19 r 26(1)
- Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, a party must apply for such permission from appellate Court and file and serve the application and documents on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the lower Court’s decision.

Appellant’s application for permission by OA or in summons (if appeal is pending before Appellate court)
O 19 r 35(1)
- Every application to the appellate Court must be made either by originating application or, in an appeal which is pending before the appellate Court, by summons
=> Applicant can file and serve and affidavit in support of the application 

Documents to be filed in Appellant’s application for permission	
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 19 r 26(7)
- Appellant for permission under this Rule:
a. Must, at the time of filing the application, file written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
b. May, at the time of filing the application, file a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits

Prohibition on filing affidavits for application for permission to appeal
O 19 r 26(15)
- No affidavit is to be filed without permission of the appellate court 

Documents must be served on all interested parties 
O 19 r 26(9)
- The application, written submissions, any accompanying bundles of authorities and bundles of documents must be served on all parties who have an interest in the appeal

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 19 r 26(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 19 r 26(11))
=> O 19 r 26(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 26(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 26(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(1) Written submission in an application to Appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD
