(3) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD
Optional – Alters time to file and serve application for permission: Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before (1) Time of extraction of judgement (2) 15th day after decision (3) Filing of application for Court’s permission 
O 19 r 26(2)
- Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before: Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, the Judge who made the decision may hear further arguments in respect of the decision if any party to the hearing, or the Judge, requests for further arguments pursuant to section 29B of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act before the earliest of the following:
a. Time which judgement is extracted: The time at which the judgment or order relating to the decision is extracted;
b. 15th day after decision: The 15th day after the date on which the decision is made;
c. Filing of application for permission: The time at which an application for permission to appeal against the decision is filed.

If request for Further Arguments made => Appellant can only file and serve application for permission within 14 days after Lower Court affirms/varies/sets aside decision after hearing Further Arguments or certifies that no Further Arguments are required
Application to appellate Court for permission when lower Court makes request for Further Arguments
O 19 r 26(3)
- If a request for further arguments in respect of a decision has been made under paragraph (2):
a. An application for permission to appeal against the decision may not be filed against the decision until the lower Court:
(i) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(ii) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required; and
b. The party seeking to apply for permission to appeal must file and serve the application for permission to appeal against the decision, and the documents mentioned in paragraph (7), within 14 days after the date the lower Court:
(i) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(ii) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required
Step 2: Appellant must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Appellant files the application 
O 19 r 35(6)
- The party who files an originating application or a summons to the appellate Court must provide security for the opposing party’s costs of the application and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time that party files the application

Form of Security 
O 19 r 35(9)
- Security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent OR
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General 
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties

Amount of Security 
O 19 r 35(10)
- Applicant must provide security in the amount of $5,000 

O 19 r 35(12)
- Appellate court may order further security for costs to be given 
Step 3: Respondent must file and serve affidavit in reply on Applicant and other parties within 14 days after Appellant serves OA and affidavit on Respondent
O 19 r 35(4)
- If the opposing party wishes, opposing party must file and serve an affidavit in reply on the applicant and other parties within 14 days after the date of application and affidavit is served on the respondent 

Documents to be filed by Respondent opposing application for permission 
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 19 r 26(8) 
- A party who wishes to oppose an application for permission under this Rule:
a. Must file and serve written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
b. May, together with the written submissions mentioned in sub?paragraph (a), file and serve a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits,

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 19 r 26(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 19 r 26(11))
=> O 19 r 26(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 26(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 26(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(1) Written submission in an application to Appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of Lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(3) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents 
Respondent must file and serve within 14 days after Appellant’s application is made
O 19 r 26(8)
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 14 days after the application for permission is made by the Appellant
Step 4: Appellant/Respondent party file written submissions and bundle of authorities 14 days after Respondent’s affidavit in reply is filed and served 

Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 19 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.

Instructions for Documents 
Must be subject to page limits 
O 19 r 37(2)
- Written submissions are subject to page limit of 35 pages
=> O 19 r 37(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 37(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 37(3)(b)

Contents of Written submissions 
O 19 r 37(6)
- The concluding paragraphs of the written submissions must include:
a. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made in the application; and
b. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the application.

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
Applicant/Respondent must file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities within 14 days after Opposing party’s affidavit in reply is filed and served
O 19 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served
Step 5: If Appellant gets permission to appeal, Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 

If approve permission => Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 
O 19 r 26(17)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 19 r 26(18)
- Appellate Court can extend at any time: Appellate Court can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal 

Other rules 
- O 19 r 26(16): No oral arguments are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders 
- O 19 r 26(15): No affidavit are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders

*Part 1B: If Court’s permission is not required – Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 28 days of Lower Court’s decision (another timeline if Request for Further Arguments made) 
O 19 r 25(1) 
- File and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties: A party who intends to appeal to the Appellate Court against the judgement of a lower Court must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal a notice of appeal in Form 35:
a. Within 28 days of lower Court’s decision; OR
b. If Request for Further Arguments has been made – Within 28 days after date in s29B(4)(b) of SCJA: In a case where a request for further arguments has been made under s29B(2) of the SCJA, within 28 days after the date mentioned in s29B(4)(b) of SCJA 

Time extension for filing and service of Notice of Appeal  
O 19 r 25(2)
- Appellate Court can extend at any time: Appellate Court can extend time for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made at any time 
- Lower Court can extend before time expires: Lower Court can extend for filing and service of Form 35 on appellant’s application made before the time expires  

Part 2: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 19 r 27(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 19 r 27(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 19 r 27(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the amount of $20,000

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 19 r 27(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 19 r 27(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 3: Appellant must wait for Lower Court to confirm record of decision 
Lower Court must give written grounds of decision after Appellant files Notice of Appeal  
Lower Court must give written grounds of decision after Form 35 is filed 
O 19 r 30(1)
- Lower Court must issue its written grounds of decision after the notice of appeal has been filed if Lower Court has not already done so 

Registry will notify parties when record of proceedings ready for collection
O 19 r 30(2)
- The Registry must notify the parties when the record of proceedings is ready for collection.

If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks of filing Notice of Appeal => Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal and for a copy of record of proceedings 
O 19 r 30(3)
- If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the date of filing of the notice of appeal, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal and for a copy of the record of proceedings

Part 4: Appellant files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Record of Appeal, (2) Appellant’s Case, (3) Appellant’s core bundle of documents, (4) Appellant’s bundle of authorities
O 19 r 30(4)
- Appellant must file and serve: 
a. Record of appeal 
b. Appellant’s Case
c. Appellant’s core bundle of documents, with the written judgement or grounds of decision of the Lower Court and the extracted order of the Lower Court in a separate volume 
d. Appellant’s bundle of authorities 

Instructions for Appellant’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Appellant’s Case – 55 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(a))
- Appellant’s core bundle of documents (excluding the written judgment or grounds of decision of the lower Court and the extracted order of the lower Court) — 55 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(a))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Case 
O 19 r 31(1)
- Appellant’s Case must contain the following: 
a. Succinct summary of the facts, the decision of the Lower Court, contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the Appellate Court;
b. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the Lower Court;
c. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)) and the appellant’s core bundle of documents
d. In the concluding paragraphs of the appellant’s Case
(i) Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal; and
(ii) Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
e. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor

Formatting requirements for written submissions 
Para 120 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Formatting requirements: 
a. The cover page(s), which are mandatory, must be included at the beginning of the document;
b. If a table of contents is mandatory under paragraph 119(4) of these Practice Directions, the table of contents must be included at the beginning of the document immediately after the cover page(s);
c. All pages must be paginated, with the page numbers corresponding to the Portable Document Format (PDF) version of the document;
d. The minimum font size to be used is Times New Roman 12 or its equivalent;
e. The print of every page must be double-spaced; and
f. Every page must have a margin on all 4 sides, each of at least 35 mm in width.

Preparation of records of appeal, written Cases and core bundles
Para 121 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Instructions for:
(1) Arrangement of appeal records and supplemental record of appeal
(2) Manner of pagination 
(3) Table of contents 
(4) Line spacing
(5) Arrangement of core bundle of documents
(6) Contents page for core bundle of documents
(7) Contents of core bundle of documents
(8) Solicitor’s responsibility for good order and completeness of appeal records 
(9) Parties must not exhibit superfluous, irrelevant or duplicative documents 
(10) Written submissions referring to any document must describe it in such a manner to allow Court to identify the nature of the document e.g. (a) Joint Venture Agreement between Party A and Party B dated 1 December 2017; (b) Minutes of meeting held on 1 December 2017 between Party A and Party B; and (c) Email dated 1 December 2017 from Party A to Party B.

Filing of appeal records and provisions of hard and soft copies 
Para 122 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Filing must be done electronically 
- Documents which need not be electronically filed: Record of appeal and supplemental record of appeal, bundle of authorities (Only list of authorities need to be filed electronically) 
- Tender hard copies of written submissions and bundles of authorities to the Registry 
- Tender soft copies of written submissions and bundles of authorities in PDF and CD-ROM

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve documents
Within 8 weeks after Registry informs parties that record of proceedings available 
O 19 r 30(4)
- Appellant must file and serve documents within 8 weeks after the date on which the Registry informs the parties that the record of proceedings is available

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 19 r 30(6)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the record of appeal (including, where required under paragraph (5)(a), the supplemental record of appeal), the core bundle of documents or the appellant’s Case within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 19 r 30(10)
- Where the respondent fails to file and serve the respondent’s Case within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Part 5: Respondent files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Respondent must file (1) Respondent’s Case, (2) Respondent’s core bundle of documents, (3) Respondent’s bundle of authorities
O 19 r 30(9)
- Respondent must file and serve: 
a. Respondent’s Case
b. Respondent’s core bundle of documents (if necessary) 
c. Respondent’s bundle of authorities

Instructions for Respondent’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Respondent’s Case – 55 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(b))
- Respondent’s core bundle of documents — 35 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(b))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Respondent’s Case 
O 19 r 31(2)
- Respondent’s Case must contain the following: 
a. A succinct summary of the contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the Appellate Court;
b. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the Lower Court;
c. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)) and the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any);
d. If the respondent intends to submit that:
(i) The Lower Court’s decision should be varied should the appeal be wholly or partially allowed where the respondent has not appealed against the decision of the GDHC; or
(ii) The lower Court’s decision should be affirmed on grounds other than those relied upon by that Court,
those submissions and the reasons for the respondent’s submissions;
e. In the concluding paragraphs of the respondent’s Case:
(i) Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal; and
(ii) Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
f. Name and signature of the respondent’s solicitor.

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents
Within 28 days after Appellant serving documents
O 19 r 30(9) 
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 28 days after Appellant serves documents mentioned in r 30(4)

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 19 r 30(6)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the record of appeal (including, where required under paragraph (5)(a), the supplemental record of appeal), the core bundle of documents or the appellant’s Case within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 19 r 30(10)
- Where the respondent fails to file and serve the respondent’s Case within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Part 6: Appellant files and serves Reply
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Appellant’s Reply, (2) Appellant’s Second Core Bundle and (2) Appellant’s Bundle of Authorities 
O 19 r 30(11)
- Appellant must file and serve:
a. Appellant’s Reply (if any)
b. Second core bundle (if necessary)
c. Appellant’s second bundle of authorities (if any) 

Instructions for Appellant’s Reply
a. Must be subject to page limit 
- Appellant’s Reply – 25 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(c))
- Appellant’s second core bundle — 25 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(c))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Reply 
O 19 r 31(4)
- Appellant’s Reply must contain the following: 
a. The appellant’s detailed submissions in reply to the respondent’s submissions;
b. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)), the appellant’s core bundle of documents, the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any), and the second core bundle (if any);
c. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor.

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve Reply 
Within 14 days of Respondent serving documents
O 19 r 30(11) 
- Appellant must file and serve Reply within 14 days after the Respondent’s Case is served on the Appellant

Other instructions on documents 
Appellant’s Case, Respondent’s Case and Appellant’s Reply must be self-contained
O 19 r 31(5)
- The appellant’s Case, the respondent’s Case and the appellant’s Reply must contain everything that the parties intend to put forward at the appeal and must be prepared on the basis that there will be no need to supplement or to elaborate on any points made.

No other documents allowed
O 19 r 30(20)
- No documents other than what have been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the General Division otherwise orders.

Order 19: Appeals from Disciplinary Tribunal under Medical Registration Act  

Interlocutory Applications/Applications on appeal 
Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 18 appeal
- Used to apply for permission from ADHC/CA to appeal from GDHC to ADHC/CA 
- Used to apply for interlocutory applications from ADHC/CA

Step 1: Applicant must make application by OA or in summons (if an appeal is pending before Appellate Court) 
O 18 r 35(1)
- Every application to the appellate Court must be made either by originating application or, in an appeal which is pending before the appellate Court, by summons
=> Applicant can file and serve and affidavit in support of the application 

Whenever application may be made to Lower Court or Appellate Court => It should be made in first instance to Lower Court => Unless impossible or impracticable 
O 18 r 35(2) 
- Whenever under these Rules an application may be made either to the lower Court or to the appellate Court, it must not be made in the first instance to the appellate Court, except where there are special circumstances which make it impossible or impracticable to apply to the lower Court.

Step 2: Applicant must provide security for opposing party’s costs 
Applicant must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Applicant files the application

Form of Security 
O 18 r 35(8)
- Security must be
d. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent OR 
e. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; OR 
f. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 35(9)
- Applicant must provide security in the amount of $5,000 

Step 3: Opposing party must file and serve Affidavit in reply on Applicant and other parties 
Opposing Party must file and serve affidavit in reply on Applicant and other parties within 14 days after Applicant serves OA and affidavit on Respondent
O 18 r 35(4)
- If the opposing party wishes, opposing party must file and serve an affidavit in reply on the applicant and other parties within 14 days after the date of application and affidavit is served on the respondent

Type of Documents to be filed

Instructions for Documents

=> O 18 r 37(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 37(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 37(3)(b)

Contents of Written submissions 
O 18 r 37(6)
- The concluding paragraphs of the written submissions must include:
c. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made in the application; and
d. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the application.

Timeline for Appellant/Opposing party to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
Applicant/Opposing party must file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities within 14 days after Opposing party’s affidavit in reply is filed and served

- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.

O 19 r 35(4)

Step 4: Applicant/Opposing party file written submissions and bundle of authorities 
Type of Documents to be filed

Application to strike out notice of appeal
Applications to strike out notice of appeal (Order 18)
Respondent must make application to Appellate Court by OA or summons supported by affidavit 
O 18 r 35(12)
- Any application to the appellate Court to strike out a notice of appeal must be made by summons supported by affidavit stating the grounds of the application.

Respondent must file and serve on Appellant within 14 days after Notice of Appeal 
O 18 r 35(13)
- The summons and the supporting affidavit mentioned in paragraph (12) must be filed and served by the applicant on the parties to the application within 14 days after service of the notice of the appeal on the applicant.

Appellant must file and serve affidavit in reply within 14 days after Respondent serves OA/summons and affidavit 
O 18 r 35(14)
- A party to the application mentioned in paragraph (12), who wishes to reply to the applicant’s affidavit, must file and serve that party’s affidavit in reply, on the applicant and the other parties to the application, within 14 days after service of the applicant’s summons and affidavit on that party

Applications to strike out notice of appeal (Order 19)
Respondent must make application to Appellate Court by OA or summons supported by affidavit 
O 19 r 35(13)
- Any application to the appellate Court to strike out a notice of appeal must be made by summons supported by affidavit stating the grounds of the application.

Respondent must file and serve on Appellant within 14 days after Notice of Appeal 
O 19 r 35(14)
- The summons and the supporting affidavit mentioned in paragraph (13) must be filed and served by the applicant on the parties to the application within 14 days after service of the notice of the appeal on the applicant.

Appellant must file and serve affidavit in reply within 14 days after Respondent serves OA/summons and affidavit 
O 19 r 35(15)
- A party to the application mentioned in paragraph (13), who wishes to reply to the applicant’s affidavit, must file and serve that party’s affidavit in reply, on the applicant and the other parties to the application, within 14 days after service of the applicant’s summons and affidavit on that party.

**Allocation of appeals between ADHC and CA
GENERAL Rule: Appeals against decisions of GDHC are usually made to the ADHC
S29C(1) SCJA
- Subject to s29C(2), an appeal against a decision of the General Division in the exercise of its original or appellate civil jurisdiction, whether under this Act or any other written law, is to be made to the Appellate Division.
	
Exception: If Sixth Schedule applies – Appeals against decisions of GDHC will be made to the CA
S29C(2) SCJA
- An appeal against a decision of the General Division is to be made to the Court of Appeal if the Sixth Schedule or any other written law so provides

Sixth Schedule of SCJA – Appeal to CA
a. Constitutional/Administrative law: The appeal arises from a case relating to constitutional or administrative law (even if the appeal does NOT raise any issue relating to constitutional or administrative law); --> FOCUS ON THE NATURE OF THE CASE ITSELF, AS IT WAS BEFORE THE GENERAL DIVISION – DOES NOT MATTER IF THE POINT ITSELF IS APPEALED
b. Contempt of Court: The appeal arises from a case relating to contempt of court (even if the appeal does not raise any issue relating to the law of contempt of court);
c. Law of arbitration: The appeal arises from a case relating to the law of arbitration (even if the appeal does not raise any issue relating to the law of arbitration);
d. Insolvency, restructuring or dissolution: The appeal arises from a case relating to the insolvency, restructuring or dissolution of a corporation, limited liability partnership or sub?fund of a variable capital company (even if the appeal does not raise any issue relating to the law concerning the insolvency, restructuring or dissolution of a corporation, limited liability partnership or sub?fund of a variable capital company);
e. Law of patents: The appeal arises from a case relating to the law of patents (even if the appeal does not raise any issue relating to the law of patents);
f. Decision of SICC: The appeal is against a decision of the Singapore International Commercial Court;
g. Parliamentary Elections Act: The appeal is against a decision or order of a Judge sitting in the General Division made under the Parliamentary Elections Act 1954;
h. Presidential Elections Act: The appeal is against a judgment or order in an action brought under section 47(8) of the Presidential Elections Act 1991;
i. The appeal is made under any of the following written laws:
(i) Section 32(1) of the Administration of Justice (Protection) Act 2016;
(ii) Sections 21A(1), 45(7) and 49(11) of the Arbitration Act 2001;
(iii) Section 74(4) of the Competition Act 2004;
(iv) Section 10(4) of the International Arbitration Act 1994;
(v) Section 18(5) of the Maintenance of Parents Act 1995;
(vi) Section 90(3) of the Patents Act 1994;
(vii) Section 35(4) of the Personal Data Protection Act 2012 as in force immediately before 1 February 2021 or section 48R(4) of the Personal Data Protection Act 2012, as the case may be;
(viii) Sections 17(8), 29(9), 35(7) and 44(9) of the Protection from Online Falsehoods and Manipulation Act 2019;
j. The appeal is made under any written law that provides for the appeal to lie to the Court of Appeal
k. The appeal is against a decision or an order of the General Division under the Mediation Act 2017, including a decision of the General Division to record or refuse to record a mediated settlement agreement as an order of court under that Act;
l. The appeal is against a decision or an order of the General Division under the Singapore Convention on Mediation Act 2020, including a decision of the General Division granting permission or refusing to grant permission to record an international settlement agreement as an order of court under that Act.

Reason for appeals identified under Sixth Schedule to be heard by CA instead of ADHC
Noor Azlin binte Abdul Rahman & Anor v Changi General Hospital [2021] SGCA 5
- Split into ADHC and CA is designed to enable ADHC to share in CA’s caseload by hearing civil appeals against GDHC divisions 
- Reasons for appeals identified under Sixth Schedule to be heard by CA: 
a. The appeals are likely to have substantial consequences for individuals or society
b. The appeals may involve questions of law of public interest which would benefit from guidance of the apex court in Singapore 
c. The appeals concern the general administration of justice 
d. The appeals involve novel questions of law or new areas of law which would benefit from guidance from CA 
e. The appeals may involve issues that are likely to be important and require earlier clarification from the CA
f. The appeals relate to strategic areas that would benefit from the stature of the apex court, such as the areas of laws which seek to bolster Singapore’s status as a dispute resolution hub or debt restructuring hub 
On when a case is “a case relating to” a specified subject matter in paragraphs 1(a)-(e) of Sixth Schedule SCJA
Seow Fook Sen Aloysius v Rajah & Tann Singapore
- The appeals which the Sixth Schedule provides are to be made to the Court of Appeal by default can be classified into three categories:
(a) First, where the appeal “arises from a case relating to” specified subject matter, such as constitutional or administrative law, contempt of court, the law of arbitration, insolvency or the law of patents. This is provided for in paras 1(a)-(e) of the Sixth Schedule. Importantly, as the words in parentheses in paras 1(a)-(e) make clear, even if the appeal itself does not raise issues relating to specified subject matter, so long as it “arises from a case relating to” that subject matter, it will nevertheless come within the Sixth Schedule.
(b) Second, where the appeal is against particular decisions of the General Division, such as a decision of the Singapore International Commercial Court (“SICC”) (see para 1(f)), a decision made under the Parliamentary Elections Act 1954 (see para 1(g)), a judgment or order made in an action brought under s 47(8) of the Presidential Elections Act 1991 (see para 1(h)), or a decision made under the Mediation Act 2017 or the Singapore Convention on Mediation Act 2020 (see paras 1(k) and (l)).
(c) Third, where the appeal is to be made to the Court of Appeal under written laws (see paras 1(i) and (j)).

- What is clear is that Parliament could NOT have intended for the criteria in paras 1(a)-(e) to be satisfied so long as the specified subject matter features somewhat by way of factual background to the “case”, even if this is by way of the most tenuous or tangential manner (it follows, of course, that the said criteria would clearly not be satisfied if the specified subject matter does not even feature in the factual background to the “case” itself). In our view, there must be something more. Otherwise, the criteria in paras 1(a)-(e) would have an exceedingly low threshold that can be satisfied in almost every instance, and which may, as a result, no longer operate to draw a distinction between those appeals which necessarily must be heard by the Court of Appeal and those which fall outside of that category. Unlike the other subparagraphs within the Sixth Schedule, the criteria in paras 1(a)-(e) cannot be read as involving a purely factual inquiry because doing so would undermine the role of paras 1(a)-(e) in carving out specific categories or types of proceedings to be heard by the Court of Appeal

- We consider that “a case relating to” a specified subject matter in paras 1(a)-(e) is one where the latter is legally relevant to and/or has some bearing on the reliefs or orders which were sought at first instance

- At the very least, some reasonable relationship must be established between the specified subject matter and the “case” from which the appeal arises, whether with regard to the legal issues therein or the application of the law to its facts, in the court below, so that either or both of which may arise for consideration in the appeal. 

- For example, in the context of para 1(d), with which we are presently concerned, the “case” from which the appeal arises must concern a fact situation which involved the rules and principles relating to the law of insolvency, so that in the appeal, the Court of Appeal is also either called upon to decide a principle or rule relating to the law of insolvency (thereafter applying it to the facts concerned), or at the very least, apply an established principle or rule relating to the law of insolvency to the facts

- *The only criteria determinative of whether an appeal comes within paras 1(a)-(e) is whether it arises from “a case relating to” specified subject matter, and not the identity of the issues raised in the appeal itself. It is only consistent with the importance associated with these areas of law identified by the specified subject matter in paras 1(a)-(e) for any appeal satisfying the criteria therein to be made to the Court of Appeal by default, irrespective of the issues raised in the appeal 
--> i.e. it does not matter if the appeal turns on issues entirely unrelated to the specified subject matter, as long as the appeal has arisen from a “case” bearing the requisite relation to a specified subject matter, it is appealable to the CA

E.g. In the context of para 1(d) of the Sixth Schedule, an example will be an appeal involving the question of whether a winding-up order should be set aside on grounds entirely unrelated to the law of insolvency, such as non-disclosure of material facts or abuse of process. Notwithstanding that, the appeal will ultimately still entail the appellate court applying the established principles or rules of winding-up to the facts in determining if the winding-up order sought at first instance had been correctly made. Hence, in these situations, despite the complexion of the precise issues arising in the appeal, the appellate court will still be required to apply to the facts established principles or rules relating to the specified subject matter, in the same way that the court below had to when it granted or denied (as the case may be) the reliefs or orders sought in the “case” at first instance.



Transfer of appeals from ADHC to CA
1. Who can transfer appeal from ADHC to CA
2. Grounds of transfer 
a. Wrong filing ground
b. More appropriate ground
c. Issues on appeal 
3. Means of transferring 
4. Timelines and procedures for transfer 

Preliminary: CA has power to transfer any appeals from ADHC to CA  
CA may transfer “any appeal against GDHC decision to the ADHC” to itself
S29D(1) of SCJA
- The Court of Appeal may transfer the following appeals to itself:
a. Any appeal against any decision of the General Division that has been made to the Appellate Division;
b. Where an order under section 39A of the Land Acquisition Act 1966 is in force, any appeal made to the Appellate Division under section 29(2) or 38(2) of the Land Acquisition Act 1966.

3 Methods to trigger CA’s power under s29D(1) of SCJA
S29D(2) of SCJA
- The power in s29D(1) may be exercised by CA: 
a. Method 1: By CA own motion: On its own motion;
b. Method 2: By ADHC reference: On a reference by the Appellate Division; or
c. Method 3: By appellant/respondent: On an application to the Court of Appeal by any party to the appeal, but such an application may only be made:
(i) On the ground that the appeal was not made to the Appellate Division in accordance with section 29C; or
(ii) On grounds prescribed by the Rules of Court.

If Method 1 and Method 2 => 3 Grounds of Transfer 
S29D(3) => O 18 r 40(2)/O 19 r 39(2)
- Ground 1: Initial appeal to ADHC was not in accordance with s29C of SCJA (E.g. show that the matter falls under Sixth Schedule but was wrongly appealed to the ADHC) 
- Ground 2: It is more appropriate for CA than ADHC to hear the appeal 
- Ground 3: One or more of the legal issues raised in the appeal engage one or more of the matters in Sixth Schedule of SCJA 
* Difference between case that is being appealed and the issues that are being raised on appeal 

S29D(3) of SCJA
- In deciding whether to exercise powers under s29D(1), CA is to have regard to matters prescribed by Rules of Court

If Method 3 => 2 Grounds of Transfer 
S29D(2)(c)(i) 
- Ground 1: Initial appeal to ADHC was not in accordance with s29C of SCJA (E.g. show that the matter falls under Sixth Schedule but was wrongly appealed to the ADHC) 

S29D(2)(c)(ii) => O 18 r 40(1)/O 19 r 39(1) 
- Ground 2: It is more appropriate for CA than ADHC to hear the appeal 

Issue: How can Appellant/Respondent transfer appeal to ADHC to the CA? 
Step 1: s29D(2) of SCJA provides for Appellant/Respondent to transfer to CA any appeal to ADHC => Appellant/Respondent must make an application to the CA and satisfy the CA of one of the grounds of transfer in s29D(2) 
- Pursuant to s29D(1) of SCJA, the CA may transfer to itself any appeal against GDHC decision that has been made to the ADHC. The CA’s power under s29D(1) may be exercised on an application to the CA by the Appellant/Respondent. 

Step 2A: If Appellant/Respondent uses Ground 1 to transfer appeal to CA
Ground 1: Initial appeal to ADHC was not in accordance with s29C of SCJA (E.g. show that the matter falls under Sixth Schedule but was wrongly appealed to the ADHC)  
S29D(2)(c)(i) of SCJA: 
- Appellant/respondent may apply to the CA for CA to exercise its powers under s29D(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the ADHC on the ground that: 
* The appeal to ADHC was not in accordance with s29C of the SCJA 

Procedure for Ground 1 for both Order 18 and Order 19
Appellant/Respondent must make application to transfer under s29D(2)(c)(i) within 14 days after the date of service of Notice of Appeal + Application must also be made in accordance with Rule 35  
O 18 r 40(3)/O 19 r 39(3)
- An application under s29D(2)(c)(i) of SCJA must be made in accordance with Rule 35 and must be filed and served within 14 days after the date of service of the notice of appeal on all interested parties  
- TLDR: Application must be made by OA (O 18 r 35(1)/O 19 r 35(1))

Move to section above on “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 18 appeal”, “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 19 appeal”

Step 2B: If Appellant/Respondent uses Ground 2 to transfer appeal to CA  
Ground 2: Appellant/Respondent must show that it is more appropriate for CA than ADHC to hear the appeal 
Ground 2: More appropriate ground 
s29D(2)(c)(ii) of SCJA/O 18 r 40(1)/O 19 r 39(1)
- Appellant/respondent may apply to the CA for CA to exercise its powers under s29D(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the ADHC on the ground that: 
* It is more appropriate for the CA than the ADHC to hear the appeal  

Factors considered to determine whether it is more appropriate for CA than ADHC to hear appeal
O 18 r 40(5)/O 19 r 39(5)
- When determining whether it is more appropriate for CA to hear an appeal that has been made to the ADHC, the CA may have regard to one or more of the following matters:
a. Proceedings relate to matter of national or public importance: Whether the proceedings relate to a matter of national or public importance;
b. Appeal raises point of law of public importance: Whether the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance;
c. Complexity and novelty of issues: The complexity and novelty of the issues in the appeal;
d. Previous CA decision relevant to a point of law that is material to current matter: Whether there is a decision of the Court of Appeal in relation to a point of law raised in the appeal which may be material to the outcome of the appeal;
e. Presence of conflicting judicial decisions: Whether there are conflicting judicial decisions;
f. Significance of results of proceedings: The significance of the results of the proceedings;
g. Any other relevant matter

Noor Azlin bte Abdul Rahman v Changi General Hospital Pte Ltd [2021] SGCA 59 
Whether the proceedings relate to a matter of national or public importance
Cases that involve issues of fact and law which are of national or public importance 

The matters of national and public importance do not necessarily have to arise squarely for the Court’s determination and do not need to have a substantial bearing on the outcome of the appeal 

National and public importance means that the case will not only affect a segment of society, but has the potential to impact Singapore on a macro-level 
Whether the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance
Point of law of public importance must be a live issue which has a substantial bearing on the outcome of the appeal 
- It cannot be a hypothetical or merely theoretical question which is peripheral or irrelevant to the appeal 

Point of law is an issue that is normative in nature and would apply generally or universally to other similar situations
- Point of fact is an issue that is necessarily confined or limited to the case at hand 

Point of law of public importance 
- New questions of law of general application 
- New questions of law that involve conflicting decisions of CA or ADHC which need to be resolved so as to bring certainty to significant areas of law 
The complexity and novelty of the issues in the appeal
Issues must be live and must have a substantial bearing on the outcome of the appeal 
- It cannot be a hypothetical or merely theoretical question which is peripheral or irrelevant to the appeal 

Novelty
- Mere fact that an issue has not arisen before in the same exact form does not immediately render the issue sufficiently novel
=> All issues are novel if framed with sufficient specificity 

Complexity
- Bear in mind that the increasing complexity of mattes in CA’s docket is one of the reasons that prompted establishment of ADHC in the first place 
Whether there is a decision of the Court of Appeal in relation to a point of law raised in the appeal which may be material to the outcome of the appeal
The prior decision of the CA must have a substantial bearing on the outcome of the appeal 
- It cannot be a hypothetical or merely theoretical question which is peripheral or irrelevant to the appeal 

The significance of the results of the proceeding
No indication as to who or what the outcome matters => Limb may be satisfied if the determination of the appeal will only affect the parties concerned if the results are of substantial and critical consequence to them 
- High and exceptional degree of personal consequences

“Demonstrating some personal interest in the results of the appeal” is insufficient as it would be too broad as to be meaningless as all appeals will fulfil this limb

Procedure for Ground 2 if Order 18 case
Appellant/Respondent must make application by OA to transfer under s29D(2)(c)(ii) within 14 days after the date which parties’ written submissions are required to be filed and served under Rule 33(5)   
O 18 r 40(4)
- Application under s29D(2)(c)(ii) of SCJA must be made in accordance with Rule 35 and must be filed and served within 14 days after the date on which the parties’ written submissions are required to be filed and served under Rule 33(5) 
- TLDR: Application must be made by OA (O 18 r 35(1))

Move to section above on “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 18 appeal”

Procedure for Ground 2 if Order 19 case
Appellant/Respondent must make application by OA to transfer under s29D(2)(c)(ii) within 14 days after the date of service of Respondent’s Case 
O 19 r 39(4)
- An application under section 29D(2)(c)(ii) of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act must be made in accordance with Rule 35, and must be filed and served no later than 14 days after the date of service of the respondent’s Case.
- TLDR: Application must be made by OA (O 19 r 35(1))

Move to section above on “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 19 appeal”

Transfer of appeals from CA to ADHC
Preliminary: CA has power to transfer to ADHC any appeals to CA  
CA may transfer “any appeal to itself” to the ADHC
S29E(1) of SCJA
- The Court of Appeal may transfer the following appeals from itself to ADHC:
a. Any appeal against any decision made by the General Division in any civil cause or matter in the exercise of the original or appellate civil jurisdiction of the General Division that has been made to the Court of Appeal;
b. Any appeal made to the Court of Appeal under section 29(2) or 38(2) of the Land Acquisition Act 1966.

2 Methods to trigger CA’s power under s29E(1) of SCJA 
S29E(2) of SCJA
- The power in s29E(1) may be exercised by CA: 
a. Method 1: By CA own motion: On its own motion; 
b. Method 2: By appellant/respondent: On an application to the Court of Appeal by any party to the appeal, but such an application may only be made on the ground that the appeal was not made to the Appellate Division in accordance with section 29C;

If Method 1 and Method 2 => 3 Grounds of Transfer 
S29E(3) => O 18 r 41(1) / O 19 r 40(1)
- Ground 1: The appeal was not made to the Appellate Division in accordance with section 29C;
- Ground 2: One of the legal issues raised on appeal engage any of the matters set out in the Sixth Schedule to that Act;
- Ground 3: All of the legal issues raised on appeal in relation to the matters set out in the Sixth Schedule to that Act relate to issues of settled law

S29E(3) of SCJA
- In deciding whether to exercise powers under s29E(1), CA is to have regard to matters prescribed by Rules of Court

If Method 2 => 1 Ground of Transfer 
S29E(2)(b) 
- Ground 1: The appeal was not made to the Appellate Division in accordance with section 29C;

Issue: How can Appellant/Respondent transfer appeal from CA to the ADHC? 
Step 1: s29E(2) of SCJA provides for Appellant/Respondent to transfer to ADHC any appeal to itself => Appellant/Respondent must make an application to the CA and satisfy the CA of one of the grounds of transfer in s29E(2) 
- Pursuant to s29E(1) of SCJA, the CA may transfer to the ADHC any appeal against GDHC decision that has been made to itself. The CA’s power under s29E(1) may be exercised on an application to the CA by the Appellant/Respondent.
Step 2: If Appellant/Respondent can only use Ground 1 to transfer appeal to ADHC
Ground 1: Initial appeal to CA was not in accordance with s29C of SCJA (E.g. show that the matter does not fall under Sixth Schedule but was wrongly appealed to the CA)  
S29E(2)(b) of SCJA: 
- Appellant/respondent may apply to the CA for CA to exercise its powers under s29E(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the CA on the ground that: 
* The appeal to CA was not in accordance with s29C of the SCJA 

Procedure for Ground 1 for both Order 18 and Order 19
Appellant/Respondent must make application by OA to transfer under s29E(2)(b) within 14 days after the date of service of Notice of Appeal + Application must also be made in accordance with Rule 35  
O 18 r 41(2)/O 19 r 40(2) 
- An application under section 29E(2)(b) of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act to transfer to the Appellate Division an appeal against a decision of the General Division that has been made to the Court of Appeal:
a. Must be made in accordance with Rule 35; and
b. Must be filed and served within 14 days after the date of service of the notice of appeal on all parties who have an interest in the appeal
- TLDR: Application must be made by OA (O 18 r 35(1)/O 19 r 35(1))

Move to section above on “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 18 appeal”, “Any interim application to the ADHC or CA hearing Order 19 appeal”

Issue: How can CA transfer appeal from CA to the ADHC? 
Step 1: s29E(2) of SCJA provides CA own its own motion to transfer to ADHC any appeal to itself => CA must be satisfied of one of the grounds of transfer in the Rules of Court 

Step 2A: If CA uses Ground 1 to transfer appeal to ADHC
Ground 1: Initial appeal to CA was not in accordance with s29C of SCJA (E.g. show that the matter does not fall under Sixth Schedule but was wrongly appealed to the CA)  
O 18 r 41(1)(a)/O 19 r 40(1)(a)
- CA may own its own motion exercise its powers under s29E(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the CA on the ground that: 
* The appeal was not made to the Court of Appeal in accordance with section 29C of that Act

Step 2B: If CA uses Ground 2 to transfer appeal to ADHC 
Ground 2: Show of the legal issues raised on appeal engage any of the matters set out in the Sixth Schedule to that Act;
O 18 r 41(1)(b)/O 19 r 40(1)(b)
- CA may own its own motion exercise its powers under s29E(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the CA on the ground that:
* None of the legal issues raised on appeal engage any of the matters set out in the Sixth Schedule to that Act

Step 2C: If CA uses Ground 3 to transfer appeal to ADHC 
Ground 3: Show that all the legal issues raised on appeal in relation to matters set out in Sixth Schedule relate to issues of settled law
O 18 r 41(1)(c)/O 19 r 40(1)(c)
- CA may own its own motion exercise its powers under s29E(1)(a) of SCJA to transfer an appeal that has been made to the CA on the ground that: 
* All of the legal issues raised on appeal in relation to the matters set out in the Sixth Schedule of SCJA relate to issues of settled law
Appeal from ADHC to CA 
1. Preliminary: Ensure Time to appeal has started 
2. Step 1: Appellant must make sure appeal not precluded by Ninth Schedule of SCJA
3. Step 2A: Order 18 
4. Step 2B: Order 19 

Preliminary: Applicant must ensure that time for appealing has started to run
- See notes above 

Step 1: Appellant must ensure that the appeal is not precluded by Ninth Schedule of SCJA 
If case is within Ninth Schedule => Appellant cannot appeal ADHC’s decision to the CA   
S46 of SCJA 
- An appeal cannot be brought against a decision of the Appellate Division in the cases specified in the Ninth Schedule

Ninth Schedule of SCJA – Cases where decision of Appellate Division is not appealable 
1. An appeal cannot be brought against a decision of the Appellate Division in the following cases:
a. ADHC makes incidental direction or interim order under s40(1): A case where the Appellate Division makes an incidental direction or interim order under section 40(1);
b. ADHC makes judgment or order by consent of parties: A case where the Appellate Division makes a judgment or an order that is made by consent of the parties;
c. ADHC gives or refuses permission to appeal against GDHC decision: A case where the Appellate Division gives or refuses permission to appeal against a decision of the General Division;
d. Written law expressly provides that ADHC decision is final: A case where any written law expressly provides that the decision of the Appellate Division is final or that there is no appeal from the decision of the Appellate Division.
2. Appeal that relates only to costs or fees: An appeal that relates only to costs or fees for hearing dates cannot be brought against a decision of the Appellate Division.
1.1 ADHC decision where parties have agreed in writing and signed that ADHC decision is final – Unless party proves that ADHC decision is affected by fraud or illegality or there was a fundamental breach of natural justice in proceedings resulting in decision: An appeal cannot be brought against a decision of the Appellate Division, where the parties have agreed in writing signed by or on behalf of each party that the decision is final, unless the party seeking to appeal proves that
a. The decision is affected by fraud or illegality; or
b. There was a fundamental breach of the rules of natural justice in the proceedings resulting in the decision
1.2 An agreement mentioned in sub-paragraph (1):
a. May be made before or after the decision to which the agreement relates is made; and
b. May relate to part of a decision, in which case references in sub-paragraph (1) to a decision are to be read as references to that part of the decision.

Step 2A: Order 18 – Appellant must apply for permission from CA to appeal to the CA
S47(1) of SCJA 
- An appeal against a decision of the Appellate Division made in the exercise of its appellate civil jurisdiction may only be brought with the permission of the Court of Appeal.

Part 1: Appellant must satisfy 2 requirements for CA grant permission to appeal to CA
O 18 r 29(5)/O 19 r 26(5)
- Where permission to appeal under section 47(1) of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act is required, the Court of Appeal may grant permission to appeal against a decision of the Appellate Division, where:
a. Requirement 1: Appeal must raise point of law of public importance: The appeal will raise a point of law of public importance; AND
b. Requirement 2: It is appropriate for CA to hear the appeal considering relevant matters including: It is appropriate for the Court of Appeal to hear a further appeal, having regard to all relevant matters, including either or both of the following:
(i) Consideration 1: Whether CA decision is required to resolve point of law: Whether a decision of the Court of Appeal is required to resolve the point of law;
(ii) Consideration 2: Whether interests of administration of justice generally or in the particular case requires CA to consider the point of law: Whether the interests of the administration of justice, either generally or in the particular case, require the Court of Appeal’s consideration of the point of law

Consideration 3: Whether point of law of public importance
S47(2) of SCJA 
- Point of law of public importance: The Court of Appeal may grant permission under subsection (1) only if the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance.

S47(3) of SCJA
- In deciding whether to grant permission under subsection (1) or in determining, for the purposes of subsection (2), whether an appeal will raise a point of law of public importance, the Court of Appeal is to have regard to matters prescribed by the Rules of Court.

Principles on Requirement 1
Principle 1: CA can exercise discretion to not grant permission even if point of law of public importance
s47(4)(a) of SCJA
- The Court of Appeal is not required to grant permission under subsection (1) even if the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance; and
 
Principle 2: “point of law of public importance” has a very high threshold 
Noor Azlin bte Abdul Rahman v Changi General Hospital Pte Ltd [2021] SGCA 59 
- In vast majority of cases, ADHC will serve as the final appellate Court 
- However, ADHC is not the apex court and some of its decisions can be subject to appeal to the CA only if leave is granted by the CA under s47 of the SCJA on the basis that the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance 
- Point of law of public importance under s47 of SCJA 
a. Threshold is higher than that under O 18 r 40(5)/O 19 r 39(5) which is for transfers of appeal between ADHC and CA 
b. Threshold is higher than the principles governing applications for leave to appeal against GDHC decision 
c. Leave will only be granted in rare circumstances 
- Reason: ADHC is not a further tier of appeal that must be crossed before a matter can reach the CA, the ADHC is meant to share in the workload and not delay it 
 
Part 2: Appellant must satisfy procedure to apply for CA’s permission to appeal to CA

Procedure is found in O 18 r 29 + O 18 r 35Step 1: Appellant must file and serve application (by OA or in summons if appeal is pending) on Appellate Court and interested parties within 14 days after Lower Court’s decision 
O 18 r 29(1)
- Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, a party must apply for such permission from appellate Court and file and serve the application and documents on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the lower Court’s decision

Appellant’s application for permission by OA or in summons (if appeal is pending before Appellate court)
O 18 r 35(1)
- Every application to the appellate Court must be made either by originating application or, in an appeal which is pending before the appellate Court, by summons
=> Applicant can file and serve and affidavit in support of the application 

Documents to be filed in Appellant’s application for permission
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 18 r 29(7)
- Appellant for permission under this Rule:
c. Must, at the time of filing the application, file written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
d. May, at the time of filing the application, file a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits

Documents must be served on all interested parties 
O 18 r 29(9)
- The application, written submissions, any accompanying bundles of authorities and bundles of documents must be served on all parties who have an interest in the appeal

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 18 r 29(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 18 r 29(11))
=> O 18 r 29(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 29(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 29(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(2) Written submission in an application to appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(4) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD
Optional – Alters time to file and serve application for permission: Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before (1) Time of extraction of judgement (2) 15th day after decision (3) Filing of application for Court’s permission 
O 18 r 29(2)
- Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before: Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, the Judge who made the decision may hear further arguments in respect of the decision if any party to the hearing, or the Judge, requests for further arguments pursuant to section 29B of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act before the earliest of the following:
d. Time which judgement is extracted: The time at which the judgment or order relating to the decision is extracted;
e. 15th day after decision: The 15th day after the date on which the decision is made;
f. Filing of application for permission: The time at which an application for permission to appeal against the decision is filed.

If request for Further Arguments made => Appellant can only file and serve application for permission within 14 days after Lower Court affirms/varies/sets aside decision after hearing Further Arguments or certifies that no Further Arguments are required
O 18 r 29(3)
- If a request for further arguments in respect of a decision has been made under paragraph (2):
c. An application for permission to appeal against the decision may not be filed against the decision until the lower Court:
(iii) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(iv) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required; and
d. The party seeking to apply for permission to appeal must file and serve the application for permission to appeal against the decision, and the documents mentioned in paragraph (7), within 14 days after the date the lower Court:
(iii) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(iv) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required.
Step 2: Appellant must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Appellant files the application 
O 18 r 35(5)
- The party who files an originating application or a summons to the appellate Court must provide security for the opposing party’s costs of the application and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time that party files the application
Form of Security 
O 18 r 35(8)
- Security must be
g. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent OR 
h. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; OR 
i. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 35(9)
- Applicant must provide security in the amount of $5,000 
Step 3: Respondent must file and serve affidavit in reply on Appellant and other parties within 14 days after Appellant serves OA and affidavit on Respondent
O 18 r 35(4)
- If the opposing party wishes, opposing party must file and serve an affidavit in reply on the applicant and other parties within 14 days after the date of application and affidavit is served on the respondent 

Documents to be filed by Respondent opposing application for permission 
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 18 r 29(8) 
- A party who wishes to oppose an application for permission under this Rule:
c. Must file and serve written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
d. May, together with the written submissions mentioned in sub?paragraph (a), file and serve a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits,

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 18 r 29(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 18 r 29(11))
=> O 18 r 29(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 29(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 29(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(1) Written submission in an application to Appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of GDHC must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(5) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents 
Respondent must file and serve within 14 days after Appellant’s application is made
O 18 r 29(8)
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 14 days after the application for permission is made by the Appellant
Step 4: Appellant/Respondent file written submissions and bundle of authorities 14 days after Respondent’s affidavit in reply is filed and served 

Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.

Instructions for Documents 
Must be subject to page limits 
O 18 r 37(2)
- Written submissions are subject to page limit of 35 pages
=> O 18 r 37(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 37(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 37(3)(b)

Contents of Written submissions 
O 18 r 37(6)
- The concluding paragraphs of the written submissions must include:
e. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made in the application; and
f. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the application.

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
Applicant/Respondent must file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities within 14 days after Respondent’s affidavit in reply is filed and served
O 18 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.
Step 5: If Appellant gets permission to appeal, Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 

If approve permission => Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 
O 18 r 29(17)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 18 r 29(18)
- Appellate Court can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal on appellant’s application made at any time 

Other rules 
- O 18 r 29(16): No oral arguments are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders 
- O 18 r 29(15): No affidavit are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders

Part 3: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 18 r 30(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 18 r 30(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 18 r 30(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the amount of $15,000

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 18 r 30(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 18 r 30(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 4: Appellant must wait for Lower Court to confirm record of decision 
Lower Court may either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision 
Lower Court either give summary of decisions or written grounds of decision 
O 18 r 33(1)
- The Lower Court may give a summary of the points he or she has decided without the need to issue written grounds of decision.

Lower Court must issue certification within 14 days of Appellant filing Notice of Appeal   
O 18 r 33(2)
- The Lower Court must certify within 14 days after the filing of the notice of appeal: 
a. Certification that lower Court already issued written grounds: That Lower Court has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision;
b. Certification that lower Court intends to issue written grounds: That Lower Court intends to issue written grounds of decision; or
c. Certification that official record of hearing is sufficient: That the certified transcript of the official record of the hearing sets out Lower Court grounds of decision sufficiently,
and if Lower Court does not do so, it is presumed that no further written grounds of decision will be issued.

If Lower Court intends to issue written grounds => Lower Court must do so as soon as possible => If not issued within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal
O 18 r 33(3)
- If Lower Court intends to issue written grounds: If the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that it will issue written grounds of decision:
a. Lower Court must do so as soon as practicable: Lower Court must endeavour to do so as soon as it is practicable; and
b. If Lower Court does not issue within 12 weeks, Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal: If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the certification, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal.

Part 5: Appellant/Respondent files written submissions, bundle of authorities
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 18 r 33(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions on why the Lower Court’s decision is to be upheld, set aside or varied 
- Appellant/Respondent must file bundle of authorities accompanying the written submissions 

No other documents may be filed => Unless Appellate Court allows 
O 18 r 33(11)
- No documents other than what has been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the appellate Court otherwise orders

Instructions for written submissions 
a. Must include appropriate costs orders 
b. Must be subject to page limit 
O 18 r 33(6)
- Written submissions:
* Must include submissions on appropriate costs orders to be made in appeal 
* Must be subject to a page limit of 35 pages 
=> O 18 r 33(16): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 18 r 33(17): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 33(16)(b)

Formatting requirements for written submissions 
Para 120 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 
- Formatting requirements: 
a. The cover page(s), which are mandatory, must be included at the beginning of the document;
b. If a table of contents is mandatory under paragraph 119(4) of these Practice Directions, the table of contents must be included at the beginning of the document immediately after the cover page(s);
c. All pages must be paginated, with the page numbers corresponding to the Portable Document Format (PDF) version of the document;
d. The minimum font size to be used is Times New Roman 12 or its equivalent;
e. The print of every page must be double-spaced; and
f. Every page must have a margin on all 4 sides, each of at least 35 mm in width.

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
O 18 r 33(5)
- Appellant/Respondent must file written submissions and bundle of authorities with the following timeline:
a. If r 33(2)(a) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court’s certification: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(a) that it has already issued a written judgment or grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Registrar;
b. If r 33(2)(b) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court notifying that written grounds are ready for collection: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(b) that it intends to issue written grounds of decision, within 14 days after the Registry notifies that a copy of the written grounds of decision is ready for collection;
c. If r 33(2)(c) applies – within 14 days of Lower Court’s certification: Where the Lower Court certifies under paragraph (2)(c) that the certified transcript of the official record of hearing sets out its grounds of decision sufficiently, within 14 days after the Registry notifies of such certification by the Lower Court;
d. If presumed no written grounds – within 28 days of filing and service of Form 35: Where it is presumed under paragraph (2) that no further written grounds of decision will be issued, within 28 days after the filing and service of the notice of appeal;
e. If r 33(3)(b) applies – within 14 days of Registrar notifying appeal to proceed: Where the appellant has applied in writing to proceed with the appeal under paragraph (3)(b), within 14 days after the Registrar notifies that the appeal is to proceed.

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 18 r 33(12)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the written submissions within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 18 r 33(15)
- Where the respondent to the appeal fails to file and serve the written submissions for the appeal within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Step 2B: Order 19 – Appellant must apply for permission from CA to appeal to the CA
S47(1) of SCJA 
- An appeal against a decision of the Appellate Division made in the exercise of its appellate civil jurisdiction may only be brought with the permission of the Court of Appeal.

Part 1: Appellant must satisfy 2 requirements for CA grant permission to appeal to CA
O 18 r 29(5)/O 19 r 26(5)
- Where permission to appeal under section 47(1) of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act is required, the Court of Appeal may grant permission to appeal against a decision of the Appellate Division, where:
a. Requirement 1: Appeal must raise point of law of public importance: The appeal will raise a point of law of public importance; AND
b. Requirement 2: It is appropriate for CA to hear the appeal considering relevant matters including: It is appropriate for the Court of Appeal to hear a further appeal, having regard to all relevant matters, including either or both of the following:
(i) Consideration 1: Whether CA decision is required to resolve point of law: Whether a decision of the Court of Appeal is required to resolve the point of law;
(ii) Consideration 2: Whether interests of administration of justice generally or in the particular case requires CA to consider the point of law: Whether the interests of the administration of justice, either generally or in the particular case, require the Court of Appeal’s consideration of the point of law

S47(2) of SCJA 
- Point of law of public importance: The Court of Appeal may grant permission under subsection (1) only if the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance.

S47(3) of SCJA
- In deciding whether to grant permission under subsection (1) or in determining, for the purposes of subsection (2), whether an appeal will raise a point of law of public importance, the Court of Appeal is to have regard to matters prescribed by the Rules of Court.

Principles on Requirement 1
Principle 1: CA can exercise discretion to not grant permission even if point of law of public importance
s47(4)(a) of SCJA
- The Court of Appeal is not required to grant permission under subsection (1) even if the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance; and
 
Principle 2: “point of law of public importance” has a very high threshold 
Noor Azlin bte Abdul Rahman v Changi General Hospital Pte Ltd [2021] SGCA 59 
- In vast majority of cases, ADHC will serve as the final appellate Court
