- However, ADHC is not the apex court and some of its decisions can be subject to appeal to the CA only if leave is granted by the CA under s47 of the SCJA on the basis that the appeal will raise a point of law of public importance 
- Point of law of public importance under s47 of SCJA 
d. Threshold is higher than that under O 18 r 40(5)/O 19 r 39(5) which is for transfers of appeal between ADHC and CA 
e. Threshold is higher than the principles governing applications for leave to appeal against GDHC decision 
f. Leave will only be granted in rare circumstances 
- Reason: ADHC is not a further tier of appeal that must be crossed before a matter can reach the CA, the ADHC is meant to share in the workload and not delay it 
 
Part 2: Appellant must satisfy procedure to apply for CA’s permission to appeal to CA

Procedure is found in O 19 r 26 + O 19 r 35Step 1: Appellant must file and serve application (by OA or in summons if appeal is pending) on Appellate Court and interested parties within 14 days after Lower Court’s decision 
O 19 r 26(1)
- Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, a party must apply for such permission from appellate Court and file and serve the application and documents on all parties who have an interest in the appeal within 14 days after the date of the lower Court’s decision.

Appellant’s application for permission by OA or in summons (if appeal is pending before Appellate court)
O 19 r 35(1)
- Every application to the appellate Court must be made either by originating application or, in an appeal which is pending before the appellate Court, by summons
=> Applicant can file and serve and affidavit in support of the application 

Documents to be filed in Appellant’s application for permission	
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 19 r 26(7)
- Appellant for permission under this Rule:
c. Must, at the time of filing the application, file written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
d. May, at the time of filing the application, file a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits

Documents must be served on all interested parties 
O 19 r 26(9)
- The application, written submissions, any accompanying bundles of authorities and bundles of documents must be served on all parties who have an interest in the appeal

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 19 r 26(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 19 r 26(11))
=> O 19 r 26(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 26(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 26(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(2) Written submission in an application to Appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(4) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD
Optional – Alters time to file and serve application for permission: Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before (1) Time of extraction of judgement (2) 15th day after decision (3) Filing of application for Court’s permission 
O 19 r 26(2)
- Lower Court can request for Further Arguments before: Where permission to appeal against a decision is required, the Judge who made the decision may hear further arguments in respect of the decision if any party to the hearing, or the Judge, requests for further arguments pursuant to section 29B of the Supreme Court of Judicature Act before the earliest of the following:
d. Time which judgement is extracted: The time at which the judgment or order relating to the decision is extracted;
e. 15th day after decision: The 15th day after the date on which the decision is made;
f. Filing of application for permission: The time at which an application for permission to appeal against the decision is filed.

If request for Further Arguments made => Appellant can only file and serve application for permission within 14 days after Lower Court affirms/varies/sets aside decision after hearing Further Arguments or certifies that no Further Arguments are required
Application to appellate Court for permission when lower Court makes request for Further Arguments
O 19 r 26(3)
- If a request for further arguments in respect of a decision has been made under paragraph (2):
c. An application for permission to appeal against the decision may not be filed against the decision until the lower Court:
(iii) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(iv) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required; and
d. The party seeking to apply for permission to appeal must file and serve the application for permission to appeal against the decision, and the documents mentioned in paragraph (7), within 14 days after the date the lower Court:
(iii) Affirms, varies or sets aside the decision after hearing further arguments; or
(iv) Certifies, or is deemed to have certified, that no further arguments are required
Step 2: Appellant must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Appellant files the application 
O 19 r 35(6)
- The party who files an originating application or a summons to the appellate Court must provide security for the opposing party’s costs of the application and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time that party files the application

Form of Security 
O 19 r 35(9)
- Security must be:
d. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent OR
e. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General 
f. In any other form acceptable to the parties

Amount of Security 
O 19 r 35(10)
- Applicant must provide security in the amount of $5,000 

O 19 r 35(12)
- Appellate court may order further security for costs to be given 
Step 3: Respondent must file and serve affidavit in reply on Applicant and other parties within 14 days after Appellant serves OA and affidavit on Respondent
O 19 r 35(4)
- If the opposing party wishes, opposing party must file and serve an affidavit in reply on the applicant and other parties within 14 days after the date of application and affidavit is served on the respondent 

Documents to be filed by Respondent opposing application for permission 
Written Submissions, Bundle of authorities, Bundle of documents
O 19 r 26(8) 
- A party who wishes to oppose an application for permission under this Rule:
c. Must file and serve written submissions and any accompanying bundle of authorities; and
d. May, together with the written submissions mentioned in sub?paragraph (a), file and serve a bundle of documents that are relevant to the application and that were filed in the proceedings below, such as the whole or a part of the notes of evidence, pleadings and affidavits,

Instructions for Documents  
Must be subject to page limit 
- Written submissions – 15 pages (O 19 r 26(10))
- Accompanying bundle of documents – 25 pages (O 19 r 26(11))
=> O 19 r 26(12): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 26(13): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 26(12)(b)

Form of Written Submission – Form 24 or Form 25  
Para 126 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
(2) Written submission in an application to Appellate Court for permission to appeal against a decision of Lower Court must be in Form 24 or Form 25 of Appendix B of PD 
(4) Written submissions must also follow formatting requirements in Para 120 of PD

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents 
Respondent must file and serve within 14 days after Appellant’s application is made
O 19 r 26(8)
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 14 days after the application for permission is made by the Appellant
Step 4: Appellant/Respondent party file written submissions and bundle of authorities 14 days after Respondent’s affidavit in reply is filed and served 

Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant/Respondent must file (1) Written Submissions and (2) Bundle of Authorities 
O 19 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served.

Instructions for Documents 
Must be subject to page limits 
O 19 r 37(2)
- Written submissions are subject to page limit of 35 pages
=> O 19 r 37(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 37(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 37(3)(b)

Contents of Written submissions 
O 19 r 37(6)
- The concluding paragraphs of the written submissions must include:
c. Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made in the application; and
d. Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the application.

Timeline for Appellant/Respondent to file written submissions and bundle of authorities  
Applicant/Respondent must file and serve written submissions and bundle of authorities within 14 days after Opposing party’s affidavit in reply is filed and served
O 19 r 37(1) 
- The applicant and the opposing party must file and serve written submissions (if any) as well as any bundle of authorities in respect of an application before the appellate Court within 14 days after the date on which the opposing party’s affidavit in reply is to be filed and served
Step 5: If Appellant gets permission to appeal, Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 

If approve permission => Appellant must file and serve Notice of Appeal (Form 35) on all interested parties within 14 days after approval 
O 19 r 26(17)
- Where permission to appeal is granted, the applicant must file and serve on all parties who have an interest in the appeal the notice of appeal in Form 35 within 14 days after the date of the Court’s decision granting permission.

Time extension for filing and service of application for permission 
O 19 r 26(18)
- Appellate Court can extend time for filing and serving an application for permission to appeal 

Other rules 
- O 19 r 26(16): No oral arguments are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders 
- O 19 r 26(15): No affidavit are to be made in an application for permission to appeal unless Appellate Court otherwise orders

Part 3: Appellant must provide security for Respondent’s costs 
Appellant file must provide security and file Certificate for Security for Cost (Form 36) at the time when Notice of Appeal is filed  
O 19 r 27(1) 
- The appellant must provide security for the respondent’s costs of the appeal and file a certificate for security for costs in Form 36 at the time the appellant files the notice of appeal.

Form of Security
O 19 r 27(4)
- The security must be:
a. In the form of a solicitor’s undertaking in Form 37 which must be filed and served on the respondent;
b. Deposited in the Registry or with the Accountant?General; or
c. In any other form acceptable to the parties.

Amount of Security 
O 19 r 27(5) 
- The appellant must provide security in the amount of $20,000

Any party can apply to Appellate Court to vary or waive amount 
O 19 r 27(6)
- Any party may apply to the appellate Court to vary or waive the amount of security for costs to be provided.

Appellate Court may order further security 
O 19 r 27(7)
- The appellate Court may order further security for costs to be given

Part 4: Appellant must wait for Lower Court to confirm record of decision 
Lower Court must give written grounds of decision after Appellant files Notice of Appeal  
Lower Court must give written grounds of decision after Form 35 is filed 
O 19 r 30(1)
- Lower Court must issue its written grounds of decision after the notice of appeal has been filed if Lower Court has not already done so 

Registry will notify parties when record of proceedings ready for collection
O 19 r 30(2)
- The Registry must notify the parties when the record of proceedings is ready for collection.

If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks of filing Notice of Appeal => Appellant must apply to proceed with appeal and for a copy of record of proceedings 
O 19 r 30(3)
- If no written grounds of decision are issued within 12 weeks after the date of filing of the notice of appeal, the appellant must apply in writing to the Registrar to proceed with the appeal and for a copy of the record of proceedings

Part 5: Appellant files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Record of Appeal, (2) Appellant’s Case, (3) Appellant’s core bundle of documents, (4) Appellant’s bundle of authorities
O 9 r 30(5) (For appeals from ADHC to CA, O 9 r 30(4) does not apply but O 9 r 30(5) applies)
- In the case of an appeal to the Court of Appeal against a decision of the Appellate Division, the record of appeal filed in the Appellate Division is treated as the record of appeal in the appeal to the Court of Appeal, and the appellant must file and serve:
a. The appellant’s supplemental record of appeal comprising:
(i) The notice of appeal to the Court of Appeal;
(ii) The certificate of payment for security for costs;
(iii) The written judgment or grounds of decision of the Appellate Division or, if there is no judgment or grounds of decision, the certified minute sheet of the Appellate Division;
(iv) The extracted order of the Appellate Division;
(v) The order granting permission to appeal to the Court of Appeal;
(vi) The parties’ Cases filed in the Appellate Division; and
(vii) All documents filed in the Appellate Division (so far as they are relevant to the matter decided and the nature of the appeal);
b. The appellant’s Case;
c. The appellant’s core bundle of documents, with the written judgment or grounds of decision of the lower Court and the extracted order of the lower Court in a separate volume; and
d. The appellant’s bundle of authorities
Instructions for Appellant’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Appellant’s Case – 55 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(a))
- Appellant’s core bundle of documents (excluding the written judgment or grounds of decision of the lower Court and the extracted order of the lower Court) — 55 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(a))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Case 
O 19 r 31(1)
- Appellant’s Case must contain the following: 
a. Succinct summary of the facts, the decision of the Lower Court, contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the Appellate Court;
b. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the Lower Court;
c. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)) and the appellant’s core bundle of documents
d. In the concluding paragraphs of the appellant’s Case
(iii) Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal; and
(iv) Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
e. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor

Formatting requirements for written submissions 
Para 120 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Formatting requirements: 
a. The cover page(s), which are mandatory, must be included at the beginning of the document;
b. If a table of contents is mandatory under paragraph 119(4) of these Practice Directions, the table of contents must be included at the beginning of the document immediately after the cover page(s);
c. All pages must be paginated, with the page numbers corresponding to the Portable Document Format (PDF) version of the document;
d. The minimum font size to be used is Times New Roman 12 or its equivalent;
e. The print of every page must be double-spaced; and
f. Every page must have a margin on all 4 sides, each of at least 35 mm in width.

Preparation of records of appeal, written Cases and core bundles
Para 121 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Instructions for:
(1) Arrangement of appeal records and supplemental record of appeal
(2) Manner of pagination 
(3) Table of contents 
(4) Line spacing
(5) Arrangement of core bundle of documents
(6) Contents page for core bundle of documents
(7) Contents of core bundle of documents
(8) Solicitor’s responsibility for good order and completeness of appeal records 
(9) Parties must not exhibit superfluous, irrelevant or duplicative documents 
(10) Written submissions referring to any document must describe it in such a manner to allow Court to identify the nature of the document e.g. (a) Joint Venture Agreement between Party A and Party B dated 1 December 2017; (b) Minutes of meeting held on 1 December 2017 between Party A and Party B; and (c) Email dated 1 December 2017 from Party A to Party B.

Filing of appeal records and provisions of hard and soft copies 
Para 122 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021
- Filing must be done electronically 
- Documents which need not be electronically filed: Record of appeal and supplemental record of appeal, bundle of authorities (Only list of authorities need to be filed electronically) 
- Tender hard copies of written submissions and bundles of authorities to the Registry 
- Tender soft copies of written submissions and bundles of authorities in PDF and CD-ROM

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve documents
Within 8 weeks after Registry informs parties that record of proceedings available 
O 19 r 30(5)
- Appellant must file and serve documents within 8 weeks after the date on which the Registry informs the parties that the record of proceedings is available

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 19 r 30(6)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the record of appeal (including, where required under paragraph (5)(a), the supplemental record of appeal), the core bundle of documents or the appellant’s Case within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 19 r 30(10)
- Where the respondent fails to file and serve the respondent’s Case within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Part 6: Respondent files documents 
Type of Documents to be filed
Respondent must file (1) Respondent’s Case, (2) Respondent’s core bundle of documents, (3) Respondent’s bundle of authorities
O 19 r 30(9)
- Respondent must file and serve: 
d. Respondent’s Case
e. Respondent’s core bundle of documents (if necessary) 
f. Respondent’s bundle of authorities

Instructions for Respondent’s documents
Must be subject to page limit
- Respondent’s Case – 55 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(b))
- Respondent’s core bundle of documents — 35 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(b))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Respondent’s Case 
O 19 r 31(2)
- Respondent’s Case must contain the following: 
g. A succinct summary of the contentions to be made at the appeal and the orders sought from the Appellate Court;
h. Detailed submissions on the facts and the legal issues, including the relevant authorities, highlighting any new points not raised in the Lower Court;
i. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)) and the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any);
j. If the respondent intends to submit that:
(iii) The Lower Court’s decision should be varied should the appeal be wholly or partially allowed where the respondent has not appealed against the decision of the GDHC; or
(iv) The lower Court’s decision should be affirmed on grounds other than those relied upon by that Court,
those submissions and the reasons for the respondent’s submissions;
k. In the concluding paragraphs of the respondent’s Case:
(iii) Submissions on the appropriate costs orders to be made on appeal; and
(iv) Submissions on the amount of costs and disbursements that should be awarded in respect of all parties to the appeal;
l. Name and signature of the respondent’s solicitor.

Timeline for Respondent to file and serve documents
Within 28 days after Appellant serving documents
O 19 r 30(9) 
- Respondent must file and serve documents within 28 days after Appellant serves documents mentioned in r 30(4)

Consequence of failure to file 
Appellant failure to file => Appeal is deemed withdrawn 
O 19 r 30(6)
- Where the appellant fails to file and serve the record of appeal (including, where required under paragraph (5)(a), the supplemental record of appeal), the core bundle of documents or the appellant’s Case within the specified time, the appeal is deemed withdrawn unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Respondent failure to file => Respondent not allowed to make submissions at appeal hearing
O 19 r 30(10)
- Where the respondent fails to file and serve the respondent’s Case within the specified time, the respondent is not allowed to make submissions at the hearing of the appeal unless the appellate Court otherwise orders.

Part 7: Appellant files and serves Reply
Type of Documents to be filed
Appellant must file (1) Appellant’s Reply, (2) Second Core Bundle and (2) Appellant’s Bundle of Authorities 
O 19 r 30(11)
- Appellant must file and serve:
d. Appellant’s Reply (if any)
e. Second core bundle (if necessary)
f. Appellant’s second bundle of authorities (if any) 

Instructions for Appellant’s Reply
a. Must be subject to page limit 
- Appellant’s Reply – 25 pages (O 19 r 32(1)(c))
- Appellant’s second core bundle — 25 pages (O 19 r 32(2)(c))
=> O 19 r 32(3): Appellate Court may allow for page limit to be exceeded (a) In special circumstances and (b) Upon payment of fees prescribed for filing of pages in excess of page limit 
=> O 19 r 32(4): Appellate Court may upon application, waive, refund, defer or apportion payment of fees in r 32(3)(b)

Contents of Appellant’s Reply 
O 19 r 31(4)
- Appellant’s Reply must contain the following: 
d. The appellant’s detailed submissions in reply to the respondent’s submissions;
e. References in the right?hand margin to the relevant pages in the record of appeal, the supplemental record of appeal (where required under Rule 30(5)(a)), the appellant’s core bundle of documents, the respondent’s core bundle of documents (if any), and the second core bundle (if any);
f. The name and signature of the appellant’s solicitor.

Timeline for Appellant to file and serve Reply 
Within 14 days of Respondent serving documents
O 19 r 30(11) 
- Appellant must file and serve Reply within 14 days after the Respondent’s Case is served on the Appellant

Other instructions on documents 
Appellant’s Case, Respondent’s Case and Appellant’s Reply must be self-contained
O 19 r 31(5)
- The appellant’s Case, the respondent’s Case and the appellant’s Reply must contain everything that the parties intend to put forward at the appeal and must be prepared on the basis that there will be no need to supplement or to elaborate on any points made.

No other documents allowed
O 19 r 30(20)
- No documents other than what have been set out in this Rule may be filed unless the General Division otherwise orders.
Evidence on Appeal
Introduction of Fresh Evidence on Appeal (Appeal hearing in ADHC) 
Parties may only give Further Evidence on Appeal in ADHC if any 2 scenarios exist 
S41(4) of SCJA
- Further evidence may only be given to ADHC in appeal hearing if: 
* Scenario 1: ADHC has given permission and on special grounds; OR 
* Scenario 2: If provided for in s41(5)

Introduction of Fresh Evidence on Appeal (Appeal hearing in CA) 
Parties may only give Further Evidence on Appeal in CA if any 2 scenarios exist 
S59(4) of SCJA
- Further evidence may only be given to CA in appeal hearing if: 
* Scenario 1: CA has given permission and on special grounds; OR 
* Scenario 2: If provided for in s59(5)

Principles underlying Scenario 1: ADHC/CA has given permission and on special grounds 
Part 1: As a general rule, the party seeking Court’s permission to admit further evidence pursuant to special grounds must satisfy 3 cumulative requirements in Ladd v Marshall 
BNX v BOE 
- The special grounds for Court to grant leave to admit further evidence in an appeal are defined by 3 cumulative conditions laid out in Ladd v Marshall:
1. Requirement 1: Non-availability at Lower Court: Evidence could not have been obtained with reasonable diligence for use in the lower Court 
=> Can be disapplied using Anan Group exception
2. Requirement 2: Relevance and materiality to the case: Evidence would probably have an important influence on the result of the case although it need not be decisive 
3. Requirement 3: Credibility or reliability of evidence: Evidence must be apparently credible, although it need not be incontrovertible 

Part 2A: However, the Court in Anan Group (Singapore) Pte Ltd has endorsed a 2-Stage framework to assess if any requirement in Ladd v Marshall can be disapplied 
Anan Group (Singapore) Pte Ltd v VB Bank (Public Joint Stock Co) 
Stage 1: Consider the nature of the proceedings below and evaluate the extent to which it bears the characteristics of a full trial and whether it more closely resembles an interlocutory appeal 
- Resembles full trial => Apply full Ladd v Marshall
- Hearing not on the merits => Apply Ladd v Marshall as a guideline 
- Hearing on interlocutory matter => First Ladd v Marshall requirement of non-availability is relaxed because interlocutory matters are “contested at an early stage of the litigation where it may be unjust to expect a party to have all his tackle in order” 
- Middle of spectrum => Consider nature of proceedings to determine if the first Ladd v Marshall condition of non-availability should be strictly applied => Nature of proceedings such as:
a. Extent to which documentary and oral evidence was adduced for the purpose of the hearing 
b. Extent to which parties had the opportunities to revisit and refine their cases before the hearing 
c. Finality of the proceedings in disposing of the dispute between the parties 

Stage 2: Consider if there are any other reasons why Ladd v Marshall should be disapplied in the interests of justice
- Whether fresh evidence reveals fraud perpetuated in lower Court 
- Whether party was prevented from adducing fresh evidence in lower Court akin to denial of natural justice
- Whether stakes of the dispute were particularly high or where there were public interests involved e.g. child welfare, criminal proceedings, judicial review cases, patent disputes 

Final balancing exercise to decide if Ladd v Marshall should be disapplied 
- Finality of proceedings and entitlement of a successful party to rely on a judgement in his favor vs Right of party to put forth relevant and credible evidence 
- Proportionality in prejudice:
a. Whether evidence sought to be adduced can be addressed by way of a reply affidavit for which any prejudice can be compensated by costs
b. Whether interests would be irreparably harm if fresh evidence is not allowed 

Part 2B: However the Court in BNX v BOE  also discussed several exceptional situations where the Court would be entitled to admit further evidence on appeal even if any of the requirements in Ladd v Marshall are not met 
BNX v BOE
- There are certain exceptional circumstances where Court would be entitled to admit further evidence on appeal even though the Ladd v Marshall criteria might not be met: 
a. Situation 1: Party denied fair opportunity to put forth relevant facts in Lower Court: Where a party has been denied a fair opportunity by the trial judge to put forth relevant facts before the Court 
b. Situation 2: Lower Court made decision on a new point which parties no opportunity to address: Where the trial judge made a decision on a new point of a substantial nature that the parties did not have the opportunity to address
c. Situation 3: Fresh evidence uncovers fraud or deception of opposing party: Where the fresh evidence uncovers fraud or deception of the other party and such fraud strikes at the very root of the litigation 

Principles underlying Scenario 2: If provided for in s41(5)/s59(5) of SCJA 
Part 1: Following s41(5)/s59(5), further evidence may be given on appeal without Court’s permission if evidence relates to matters after date of Lower Court decision 
S41(5) of SCJA 
- Such further evidence may be given to the ADHC without permission if: 
* The evidence relates to matters occurring after the date of the decision appealed against

S59(5) of SCJA 
- Such further evidence may be given to the Court of Appeal without permission if: 
* The evidence relates to matters occurring after the date of the decision appealed against

Part 2: In BNX v BOE, Court held that even though s41(5)/s59(5) may be satisfied in relation to a piece of further evidence, it can only be admitted as evidence if it satisfies 3 additional conditions in BNX v BOE
BNX v BOE
- In assessing whether further evidence produced under s41(5)/s59(5) can be admitted as evidence, the Court would have to: 
1. Condition 1: Ensure that evidence is only given for matters that occur after trial below: Ascertain what the relevant matters are, of which evidence is sought to be given and ensure that these are matters that occurred after the trial or hearing below
2. Condition 2: Ensure that evidence is at least potentially material to the issues in the appeal: Satisfy itself that the evidence of these matters is at least potentially material to the issues in the appeal
3. Condition 3: Ensure that evidence at least appears credible: Satisfy itself that the material at least appears to be credible 

Procedures to give Further Evidence on Appeal in ADHC/CA
ADHC: Oral examination in Court, Affidavit, Deposition taken before examiner or commissioner, in any other manner allowed by ADHC
S41(3)
- The ADHC may receive further evidence:
a. By oral examination in court
b. By affidavit;
c. By deposition taken before an examiner or a commissioner; or
d. In any other manner that the ADHC allows.

CA: Oral examination in Court, Affidavit, Deposition taken before examiner or commissioner, in any other manner allowed by CA
S59(3)
- The Court of Appeal may receive further evidence:
a. By oral examination in court
b. By affidavit;
=> File under O 18 r 35/O 19 r 35
c. By deposition taken before an examiner or a commissioner; or
d. In any other manner that the Court of Appeal allows.

Note: Same provisions 
O 18 r 8(6)
- Subject to any written law, the appellate Court has power to receive further evidence, either by oral examination in court, by affidavit, by deposition taken before an examiner, or in any other manner as the appellate Court may allow, but no such further evidence (other than evidence relating to matters occurring after the date of the decision appealed against) may be given except on special grounds

O 19 r 7(7) 
- Subject to any written law, the appellate Court has power to receive further evidence, either by oral examination in court, by affidavit, by deposition taken before an examiner, or in any other manner as the appellate Court may allow, but no such further evidence (other than evidence relating to matters occurring after the date of the decision appealed against) may be given except on special grounds.


*C. ENFORCEMENT OF COURT ORDERS 
Preliminary: Why should Judgement Creditor apply for Enforcement Order? 
- Enforcement Order: Enables Judgement Creditor to enforce the judgement against the Judgement Debtor by using tools like garnishee orders, seizure and sale orders etc. 

*Stay of enforcement
General rule: a court order takes effect from its date, and the filing of an appeal would NOT operate automatically to stay enforcement (O 18 r 6; O 19 r 6)

An enforcement respondent who wishes enforcement to be stayed need to apply for a stay order (via O 22 r 13 ROC), which would then be a discretionary measure for the court. It would usually require a showing of special circumstances – which go to the enforcement of the court order, and not the court order’s validity or correctness. 
- The stay order can be applied on the ground that there is a special case making it inappropriate to enforce the court order immediately (O 22 r 13(1) ROC) or pending appeal (s45(1) and 60C SCJA)
- E.g. a successful appeal could be rendered nugatory if a stay is not imposed in the mean time

Lee Kuan Yew v JBJ:
- The court’s power to grant a stay is entirely in the discretion of the court, but the discretion must be exercised in accordance with established principles
- Where a judgement was given after a FULL TRIAL (cf summary judgement or judgement in default) and an unsuccessful defendant had a full opportunity to present his case, the court should NOT deprive a successful plaintiff of the fruits of his victory pending an appeal, unless the unsuccessful defendant can show some special circumstances to justify granting of a stay
- E.g. of special circumstance: shown by affidavit that unless a stay is granted, a successful appeal could be nugatory – i.e. then the defendant would be disadvantaged if his appeal is successful. 
- There might be the likelihood of judgement creditor becoming insolvent before the disposal of the appeal, or the circumstances might be such that if the judgement debt and costs are paid (from the debtor to creditor), there is no reasonable probability of the judgement debtor getting them back if the appeal succeeds.

*Mareva injunction post-judgement to aid execution of court orders / judgement debt
JTrust Asia v Group Lease Holdings
- Conditions for the grant of a Mareva injunction post-judgement: the Court must be satisfied that – 
(a) there is a real risk of the debtor dissipating his assets with the intention of depriving the creditor of satisfaction of the judgment debt;
(b) the injunction must act as an aid to execution of court order/judgement; AND 
--> injunction will NOT be allowed for ulterior motives like to oppress the enjoined party
(c) it must be in the interests of justice to grant the injunction 
--> e.g. Judgment Sum and cost orders have already been ordered in favour of the appellant and there is no injustice in enjoining the sum required to ensure that the Judgment Sum is promptly paid to the appellant 

*Step 1: Application for Enforcement Order
Enforcement Applicant may apply to Court for Enforcement Order
O 22 r 2(1)
- An enforcement applicant may apply for an enforcement order to enforce one or more Court orders, without affecting any other methods of enforcement that are available to the enforcement applicant under any written law

Definitions 
- “property” or “properties”: Means immovable property or movable property of whatever description 
- “movable property”: Includes cash, debt, deposits of money, bonds, shares or other securities, membership in clubs or societies, and cryptocurrency or other digital currency 

Seizure and sale of shares in private company are not common because hard to value 

Procedure to apply for Enforcement Order 
Enforcement Applicant must make application any time 3 days after Court order has been served on Enforcement Respondent  
O 22 r 2(3)
- An enforcement applicant must make application not earlier than 3 days after the Court order has been served on the enforcement respondent 

Contents of application – Summons without notice + Form 38
O 22 r 2(3)
- An enforcement applicant may apply to the Court by: 
* Summons without notice for an enforcement order in Form 38 

Application must be supported by Affidavit with O 22 r 2(4) contents 
O 22 r 2(4)
- Affidavit supporting the application for an enforcement order must state:
a. The terms of the Court order;
b. The enforcement respondent’s name and address;
c. The date that the Court order was served on the enforcement respondent;
d. The terms of the Court order which have not been complied with by the enforcement respondent and which are to be enforced;
e. Where more than 6 years have passed since the date of the Court order, the reasons for the delay in the application;
f. Where any change has occurred in the identity of the enforcement applicant or the enforcement respondent since the date of the Court order, the change that has occurred;
g. If the Court order requires the enforcement respondent to pay money, the amount due to the enforcement applicant, the amount recovered from any security held by the enforcement applicant, the amount that has been paid by the enforcement respondent and the amount that remains owing;
h. If interest is payable and continues to accumulate, the amount of interest owing to the enforcement applicant daily from the time of making the affidavit;
i. If a specific property is to be seized, other than property already specified in the Court order, the description of the property and the evidence that the whole or a specified part of the property belongs to or is in the possession or control of the enforcement respondent;
j. If the specific property is not in the possession or control of the enforcement respondent, the evidence that all persons in actual possession or control of the specific property have been notified about the application for an enforcement order;
k. If a deposit of money or other debt due to the enforcement respondent from any non?party is to be attached, the description of the deposit of money or debt and the evidence that the deposit belongs to or that the debt is due to the enforcement respondent, whether immediately or at some future date or at certain intervals in the future;
l. Whether the Sheriff is to enforce the various parts of the enforcement order in any particular sequence or whether all or some parts may be enforced simultaneously; and
m. That the solicitors for the enforcement applicant (if the enforcement applicant is represented by solicitors) or the enforcement applicant (if the enforcement applicant is not represented by solicitors) undertake to:
(i) Indemnify the Sheriff against all claims, costs and expenses arising from complying with the enforcement order;
(ii) Pay upon request all charges, commissions, expenses and fees incurred by or payable to the Sheriff in complying with the enforcement order; and
(iii) Deposit the amount of money requested by the Sheriff before the Sheriff complies with the enforcement order and from time to time,
and exhibit a written undertaking stating the matters in sub?paragraph (m)(i), (ii) and (iii).

*Step 2: Effect of enforcement order
Enforcement Order authorizes Sheriff to carry out certain acts 
O 22 r 2(2) 
- An enforcement order authorizes the Sheriff to do one or more of the following (CUMULATIVE): 
a. Seizure and sale of Enforcement Respondent’s property: In respect of an enforcement order for seizure and sale of property, to seize and sell all property belonging to the enforcement respondent;
b. Seizure and delivery of Enforcement Respondent’s property: In respect of an enforcement order for delivery or possession of property, to seize and deliver or give possession of property in the possession or control of the enforcement respondent;
c. Attachment of a debt (Garnishee order) which is due to Enforcement Respondent: In respect of an enforcement order for attachment of a debt, to attach a debt which is due to the enforcement respondent from any non?party, whether immediately or at some future date or at certain intervals in the future, including where the debt which is due to the enforcement respondent is represented by a deposit of money by the enforcement respondent in a non?party that is a financial institution, whether or not the deposit has matured and despite any restriction as to the mode of withdrawal;
d. To do anything specified in the Court order

*Step 3: Validity of enforcement order
12 months beginning from date of issue of Enforcement Order
O 22 r 2(5)
- Subject to paragraph (8), an enforcement order is valid in the first instance for 12 months beginning with the date of issue

Court may extend validity by 12 months if 2 requirements are satisfied
O 22 r 2(6)
- The Court may by order extend the validity of the enforcement order from time to time for a period of 12 months at any time beginning with the day on which the order is made if:
* Requirement 1 – Enforcement costs and amount due to Enforcement Applicant have not been fully satisfied: The enforcement costs and the amount due to the enforcement applicant have not been fully satisfied or the enforcement respondent has not complied with all the terms of the Court order; and 
* Requirement 2 – Application for extension made before expiry date: An application for extension is made to the Court before the day on which the enforcement order would otherwise expire.
An enforcement order ceases to be valid, either –
O 22 r 2(8)
(a) After the enforcement applicant gives written notice to the Sheriff not to take further action, or
(b) After an order of the Court for satisfaction to be recorded is made under O 22 r 3 --> NB: any person who has satisfied a judgment debt may on filing a consent of the judgment creditor in Form 39 apply to the Court for satisfaction to be recorded, and the Court may order satisfaction to be recorded accordingly

*Carrying out of Enforcement Order by Sheriff 
Sheriff must carry out the sequence of acts indicated in enforcement order
If Enforcement Order indicates sequence of acts => Sheriff must carry out the sequence
O 22 r 6(1) 
- The Sheriff must carry out the terms of the enforcement order in the sequence indicated (if any) in the enforcement order and at the time, place and in the manner determined by the Sheriff, and may exercise any powers under any written law relating to forced entry into premises
=> Note: If judgment debtor has large known bank accounts which can satisfy the judgement debt then should sequence the attachment of debt/garnishee order first, before the seizure and sale of other properties

E.g. of Sequence 
- If Enforcement Respondent has money in banks: Enforcement order should require Sheriff to first attach debt/garnishee order before seizure and sale of money in bank 

If Enforcement Order does not indicate sequence of acts => Sheriff has discretion to decide 
O 22 r 6(2)
- If no sequence of enforcement is indicated in the enforcement order, the Sheriff may carry out its terms in any order and sequentially or concurrently, in the Sheriff’s discretion.

*Step 1: When is an Enforcement Order considered carried out? 
Acts under Enforcement OrderWhen is the act considered effected?
- i.e. when is seizure and sale of movable property considered effected 
For delivery or possession of movable property
When Sheriff: 
- Takes physical possession of movable property; OR 
- Affixes Sheriff’s seal on movable property
For seizure and sale of movable propertyWhen Sheriff: 
- Affixes Sheriff’s seal on movable property; AND 
- Serves notice of seizure on person having possession or control of movable property OR 
Leaves notice of seizure at place where movable property was seized 

See below for: 
- Form of notice of seizure 
- Rules on service of notice of seizure on Enforcement Respondent
For possession of immovable propertyWhen Sheriff: 
- Posts notice of seizure on some conspicuous part of immovable property; AND 
- Enters and takes possession of immovable property; AND 
- Serving notice of seizure on persons who are present and in actual possession or control of immovable property (if applicable)

See below for: 
- Form of notice of seizure 
- Rules on service of notice of seizure on Enforcement Respondent
For seizure and sale of immovable propertyWhen Sheriff: 
- Serves notice of seizure on Singapore Land Authority in respect of title of immovable property; AND 

When Enforcement Applicant: 
- Registers Enforcement Order under any law relating to immovable property within 14 days of service of notice of seizure by Sheriff; AND
- Gives notice in writing to Sheriff that Enforcement Order has been registered

See below for: 
- Form of notice of seizure 
- Rules on service of notice of seizure on Enforcement Respondent
For attachment of a debt due to Enforcement Respondent from a financial institution 

i.e. Garnishee Order on bank with Enforcement Respondent’s bank account 
When Sheriff: 
- Serves notice of attachment on the financial institution in respect of the deposit in such institution 

See below for: 
- Form of notice of attachment 
- Rules on service of notice of attachment on Enforcement Respondent
- Rights and obligations of non-party 
For attachment of a debt due to Enforcement Respondent from a non-party 

i.e. Garnishee Order on Enforcement Respondent’s debtor
When Sheriff: 
- Serves notice of attachment on non-party from which money is due to the Enforcement Respondent 

Regardless: Whether money is due immediately or at some future date or at certain intervals in the future 

See below for: 
- Form of notice of attachment 
- Rules on service of notice of attachment on Enforcement Respondent
- Rights and obligations of non-party 
For seizure and sale of bonds, shares, securities or membership in club
When Sheriff: 
- Serves notice of seizure on the person which registers the ownership in respect of the bonds, shares, or other securities, or which registers the membership in the club or society 

See below for: 
- Form of notice of seizure 
- Rules on service of notice of seizure on Enforcement Respondent
O 22 r 6(4)
- An enforcement order is carried out by the Sheriff:
a. In respect of an enforcement order for delivery or possession of movable property — by taking physical possession of the movable property or affixing the Sheriff’s seal on the movable property;
b. In respect of an enforcement order for seizure and sale of movable property:
(i) By affixing the Sheriff’s seal on the movable property; and
(ii) By serving a notice of seizure on the person or entity having possession or control of the movable property or leaving a notice of seizure at the place where the movable property was seized;
c. In respect of an enforcement order for the possession of immovable property — by posting a notice of seizure on some conspicuous part of the immovable property and entering and taking possession of the immovable property and, where applicable, by serving a notice of seizure on the persons who are present and in actual possession or control of the immovable property;
d. In respect of an enforcement order for seizure and sale of immovable property — by serving a notice of seizure on the Singapore Land Authority in respect of title to the immovable property, and with the enforcement applicant:
(i) Separately registering the enforcement order under any written law relating to the immovable property within 14 days after service of the notice of seizure; and
(ii) Giving notice in writing to the Sheriff that the enforcement order has been duly registered;
e. In respect of an enforcement order for attachment of a debt due to the enforcement respondent from a non?party that is a financial institution as represented by a deposit of money, whether or not the deposit has matured and despite any restriction as to the mode of withdrawal — by serving a notice of attachment on the financial institution in respect of the deposit in such institution;
f. In respect of an enforcement order for attachment of a debt due to the enforcement respondent from any other non?party — by serving a notice of attachment on the non?party from which money is due to the enforcement respondent, whether the money is due immediately or at some future date or at certain intervals in the future; or
g. In respect of an enforcement order for seizure and sale of bonds, shares or other securities or membership in a club or society — by serving a notice of seizure on the person or entity which registers the ownership in respect of the bonds, shares or other securities, or which registers the membership in the club or society.

Form of Notice of Seizure/Notice of Attachment 
Notice of Seizure/Notice of Attachment must be in Form 40 and be prepared by the Sheriff 
O 22 r 6(5) 
- The notice of seizure or attachment must be in Form 40 and may be prepared by the Sheriff

Enforcement Applicant can require Sheriff’s attendance for certain matters
Para 140 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- Enforcement applicant can require for Sheriff’s attendance: 
* At the place of execution after the first attendance to carry out enforcement order or arrest a debtor or any other purpose
* To proceed with sale of seized property 
* To release seized report 
- Enforcement applicant can do so by filling Request for Attendance of the Sheriff in Form 35 of Appendix B of these PD through the Electronic Filing Service
- Enforcement applicant has to pay fees to Sheriff under Fourth Schedule to ROC 2021 

*Step 2: After effecting seizure/attachment, Sheriff can direct Enforcement Applicant to serve copy of Notice of seizure/attachment on Enforcement Respondent 
When Seizure/Attachment has been effected => Copy of Notice of Seizure/Attachment must be served on Enforcement Respondent within 7 days after effecting of Seizure/Attachment => Unless Court order otherwise
O 22 r 6(6)
- When a seizure or attachment has been effected under paragraph (4), a copy of the notice of seizure or attachment must be served on the enforcement respondent within 7 days after effecting the seizure or attachment, unless the Court otherwise directs in the enforcement order

Methods of Service
O 22 r 6(7)
- Method 1: Personal Service under O 7 r 2 
- Method 2: Ordinary Service under O 7 r 3
- Method 3: Leaving copy of Notice of Seizure/Notice of Attachment at, or sending it by post to, the address of the place from which the property was seized

Sheriff can direct Enforcement Applicant to engage services of any lawyer to file notice and effect service of notice 
Para 141 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- After Sheriff carries out enforcement order by serving notice of seizure on any person or entity, notice of seizure on Singapore Land Authority or notice of attachment on any financial institution or non-party => Sheriff may also engage or direct enforcement applicant to engage services of any appropriate person or service provider or solicitors to file notice of seizure and effect service of such notice 

*Step 3: Rights and Obligations of non-party served with notice of attachment 
Right to claim costs of $100 from Sheriff within 14 days after service of notice of attachment => $100 is deductible from debt owed by non-party to Enforcement Respondent 
O 22 r 6(8)
- A non?party who is served with a notice of attachment is entitled to claim costs of $100 from the Sheriff but only if the claim is made within 14 days after service, and the non?party may deduct that amount from the debt owing from the non?party to the enforcement respondent which is attached under the notice of attachment prior to handing or paying over the sums mentioned in paragraph (10)

Obligation to inform Sheriff of amount owed by non-party to judgement debtor that is available to be attached within 14 days after service of notice of attachment
O 22 r 6(9)(a)
- A non?party who is served with a notice of attachment must, within 14 days after service of the notice of attachment, inform the Sheriff of the amount owing by the non?party to the enforcement respondent that is available to be attached; and

Obligation to not deal with attached amount until occurrence of certain events 
O 22 r 6(9)(b)
- A non?party who is served with a notice of attachment must not deal with the attached amount:
(i) If Rule 10 objection is filed – Until notice of objection has been determined: If a notice of objection is filed under Rule 10 — until after the notice of objection has been determined in the manner set out in that Rule; or 
(ii) In any other case – Until 21 days after service of notice of attachment: In any other case — until after 21 days have passed after the date of service of the notice of attachment

If no Rule 10 objection is filed – Obligation to hand over money to Enforcement Applicant and Sheriff within 7 days after 21 days after service of notice of attachment 
O 22 r 6(10)
- If no notice of objection is filed under Rule 10, the non?party must hand or pay over:
a. Pay to Enforcement Applicant the money initially due to Enforcement Respondent: To the enforcement applicant the money due to the enforcement respondent; and
b. Pay to Sheriff the commission due: To the Sheriff the commission due to the Sheriff,
within 7 days after the expiry of the time mentioned in paragraph (9)(b)(ii).


*Step 4: Enforcement Respondent or Non-party can object to seizure/attachment under O 22 r 10 (Rule 10 Objection)
Preliminary: Enforcement Respondent and Non-party can object 
O 22 r 10(1)
- Enforcement respondent (judgement debtor); OR 
- Any other person (usually non-party against whom garnishee order is made) 

*Part 1: Objecting Enforcement Respondent/Non-party must file and serve notice of objection within 14 days after service of the notice of seizure or attachment  
a. Notice of objection must be served to Sheriff 
b. Copy of notice of objection must be served to Enforcement Applicant, Enforcement Respondent (if not objector) and Non-party (if not objector) 
O 22 r 10(1)
- Where the enforcement respondent or any other person objects (each called in this Rule the objector) to any seizure of property or attachment of a debt by the Sheriff, the objector must within 14 days after the service of the notice of seizure or attachment:
a. Give notice of such objection to the Sheriff by filing a notice of objection; and
b. Serve a copy of the notice of objection on the enforcement applicant, the enforcement respondent (if not the objector) and any non?party served with the notice of attachment (if not the objector)

Contents of notice of objection 
O 22 r 10(2)
- The notice of objection must identify the objector, specify the property or debt in dispute, state the grounds of objection and include any evidence supporting the grounds of objection

*Part 2A: When Enforcement Applicant accepts grounds of objection, must carry out O 22 r 10(3) 
O 22 r 10(3)
- If the enforcement applicant accepts the grounds of objection: 
* Enforcement Applicant must file and serve Consent to Release (Form 37) to Sheriff and objector within 14 days after service of notice of objection: The enforcement applicant must give notice in writing to the Sheriff and the objector within 14 days after the service of the notice of objection that 
* Notice of consent releasing seizure of property or attachment of debt: the enforcement applicant consents to the release from seizure of the specified property or the release from attachment of the specified debt, 
* Sheriff must release property or debt accordingly: and the Sheriff must release the specified property or debt accordingly.

Para 142 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- If enforcement applicant consents to objection => Must within 14 days after service of notice of objection => File and serve a Consent to Release in Form 37 of Appendix B of PD on Sheriff and objector 

*Part 2B: When Enforcement Applicant disputes grounds of objection, must carry out Para 142 of SCPD
Para 142 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- Enforcement Applicant must file and serve Notice of Dispute (Form 38) to Sheriff and objector within 14 days after notice of objection: If enforcement applicant disputes objection => Must within 14 days after service of notice of objection => File and serve a Notice of Dispute in Form 38 of Appendix B of PD on Sheriff and objector 
- Within 7 days after service of Notice of Dispute to Sheriff and objector 
=> Sheriff will direct Enforcement Applicant to apply to Court by summons in Form 39 + Affidavit for an order determining the grounds of objection 
=> Enforcement Applicant must serve the summons + Affidavit on Objector, Enforcement Respondent and non-party: Within 7 days after serving of Notice of Dispute => Sheriff will direct that enforcement applicant apply to Court by summons in Form 39 of Appendix B of PD supported by affidavit for an order determining the ground of objection in respect of the property or debt in dispute => Summons and affidavit must be served on objector, enforcement respondent, non-party served with notice of attachment 

*Part 2C: When Enforcement Applicant does not respond within 14 days after service of notice of objection by objector => Sheriff may direct Objector to apply to Court for release 
O 22 r 10(4)
- If the enforcement applicant, within 14 days after the service of the notice of objection, fails to consent to the release or gives notice of dispute:
* The Sheriff may direct the objector to apply to the Court for an order to release the specified property or debt.

Procedure when Objector applies to Court for release 
O 22 r 10(5) 
- Where the Sheriff directs the objector to apply to the Court under paragraph (4), the objector must:
a. Within 7 days of Sheriff’s direction, Objector must apply to Court by summons in Form 40 + Affidavit: Apply by summons in the action supported by affidavit within 7 days after the direction, failing which the objection is deemed to have been withdrawn;
b. Objector must serve summons + Affidavit on Enforcement Applicant, Enforcement Respondent and non-party served with notice of attachment within 7 days after application to Court: Serve the summons and supporting affidavit on the enforcement applicant, the enforcement respondent (if not the objector), and any non?party served with the notice of attachment (if not the objector), within 7 days after making the application; and
c. Objector must notify Sheriff of case and application number within 7 days after application: Give notice in writing to the Sheriff of the case and application number of the summons filed, within 7 days after making the application

Para 142 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- If enforcement applicant fails to respond within 14 days of notice of objection => Sheriff direct objector to apply to Court => Objector must within 7 days after direction, file summons in Form 40 of Appendix B of PD + Affidavit => Summons and affidavit must be served on enforcement applicant, enforcement respondent and any non-party served with notice of seizure or attachment 

*Sheriff’s rights and obligations when objector objects 
Sheriff may provide information upon request 
O 22 r 10(6)
- The Sheriff may provide to the enforcement applicant, the enforcement respondent or any other person upon request such information relating to the seizure or attachment as is appropriate

Sheriff must not sell any property that is in dispute
O 22 r 10(7)
- The Sheriff must not sell any property that is in dispute

Sheriff may seek Court’s directions by letter at any time
O 22 r 10(8)
- The Sheriff may seek the Court’s directions by letter at any time.

*Can garnishee order/attachment be made over joint account held by judgement debtor and innocent party?
Previously cannot under One Investment and Consultancy Ltd
- Previously, One Investment and Consultancy Ltd [2016] SGHC 208 stood for general proposition that joint account held in the names of a judgement debtor and an innocent party jointly cannot be subject to attachment under a garnishee order 

Recently, Timing Ltd indicated that a provisional garnishee order can be issued under certain conditions to prevent judgement debtor from ring-fencing his money in the joint account  
- Recently, Timing Ltd [2020] SGHC 169 indicated that provisional garnishee orders could be issued under certain conditions => Provisional garnishee orders can prevent judgement debtor from ring-fencing his assets by transferring his funds into a joint account with a 3rd party pending determination of final garnishee order 
- Conditions: 
a. There is strong prima facie evidence that all the money in the joint account belongs to the judgement debtor
b. Notice is given to the innocent joint account holder by the show cause hearing (to determine final provisional order) 
c. Judgement creditor provides undertaking to pay any costs and reasonably foreseeable losses of garnishee or joint account holder should it be shown to the satisfaction of the court that the money in the joint account is not in fact payable in whole or in part to the judgement debtor 

Timing Ltd indicated that a final garnishee order will be issued if judgement creditor can show on a balance of probabilities that judgement debtor solely owned money in joint account 
- However, Timing Ltd [2021] SGHC 5 says that a final garnishee order can only be issued if judgement creditor shows on a balance of probabilities that:
* The judgement debtor solely owned the money in the joint account
a. Look at contributions => Look at PRT => Whether PRT rebutted by contrary intention or POA => Whether POA rebutted by contrary intention 
 
One Investment and Consultancy Ltd v Champ Poh Meng (DBS Bank Ltd, garnishee) 
- Joint account held in the names of a judgement debtor and an innocent party jointly cannot be subject to attachment under a garnishee order 
- Reasons: 
a. Prejudice to banks: 
(i) There is no framework for banks to assess each joint holder’s contributions and stake in the joint account and to require banks to make such assessment could expose them to being sued by non-party joint account holders 
(ii) Even if a framework is to be adopted, there would be increased operational and legal costs of compliance imposed on the banks => Such costs could be borne by judgement creditors and debtors => Imposing a further barrier to justice 
b. Prejudice to non-party joint account holders:
(i) There is no framework for a joint account holder to assert his share in the joint account, no requirement for innocent joint account holder to be notified and no mechanism for innocent joint account holder to seek determination of judgement debtor’s interest in the joint account => Implication: Garnishee order could be made final, and the sum specified be deducted even before the innocent joint holder is notified. Even if innocent joint holder is notified, he has no recourse other than to object to the bank or incur substantial legal cost by objecting to garnishee proceedings in Court
(ii) Even if judgement debtor’s contribution is determined as half => There is a decision to freeze half of the account was made => Judgement debtor joint account holder can just withdraw the other half that is not frozen => Innocent joint holder will be forced to shoulder the whole of the judgement debt as all that would be left is the frozen money 

Timing Ltd v Tay Toh Hin [2020] SGHC 169 
- Exception to grant provisional garnishee order: Provisional garnishee orders could be issued against joint accounts if:
a. There is strong prima facie evidence that all the money in the joint account belongs to the judgement debtor
b. Notice is given to the innocent joint account holder by the show cause hearing (to determine final provisional order) 
c. Judgement creditor provides undertaking to pay any costs and reasonably foreseeable losses of garnishee or joint account holder should it be shown to the satisfaction of the court that the money in the joint account is not in fact payable in whole or in part to the judgement debtor 
- Held: Strong prima facie case was established as judgement debtor himself admitted that the money in the joint bank accounts were paid to him personally and belonged solely to him 
- To prevent provisional garnishee order: After strong prima facie evidence is provided, judgement debtor and innocent joint account holder has evidential burden and must adduce evidence to prove the contrary 

Timing Ltd v Tay Toh Hin [2021] SGHC 5 
- Requirements to obtain final garnishee order: Final garnishee order will only be issued against joint accounts if judgement creditor shows on a balance of probabilities that the judgement debtor solely owned the money in the joint account:
a. Look at contributions => Look at PRT => Whether PRT rebutted by contrary intention or POA => Whether POA rebutted by contrary intention 
- Held: Fail to establish on a BOP that all the money in the joint account belonged beneficially to the judgement debtor: 
a. Other joint account holder is wife of judgement debtor and wife had no other accounts in Singapore which were not jointly held with judgement debtor => It would be odd in the case of a 36 year marriage where there was no separation of money between the couple if there was no mutual intent on the couple that the wife should have a beneficial interest in the money in the joint account 
b. Even though PRT for husband => There was strong POA operated in favor of the wife because of closeness of relationship between husband and wife and financial dependence of wife on husband

*Examination of Enforcement Respondent (previously called EJD – enforcement of judgement debtor)
Preliminary: Why should Judgement Creditor apply for Examination of Enforcement Respondent?  
- If judgement creditor finds it difficult to enforce judgement or enforcement order against judgement debtor because he does not know what assets the judgement debtor has => Judgement creditor can use EER to find out about the judgement debtor’s assets 

Preliminary: Check if judgement debtor has applied for a stay of enforcement of Court order pending appeal => If so, Enforcement Applicant will be precluded from applying for EER 
Reason: Application of EER is deemed to be an enforcement of Court order 
O 22 r 11(4)
- An application under this Rule is deemed to be enforcement of a Court order and is within the terms of any written law or any order staying enforcement of that Court order
=> Implication: EER cannot be enforced if there is a stay of enforcement application made by the enforcement respondent 

O 22 r 11(4) reverses previous position in case law 
- This reverses the previous position in PT Bakrie Investindo v Global Distressed Alpha Fund 1. Ltd Partnership which held that an order staying execution of a judgement pending appeal would not bar an EJD order which is depicted as a mere information-gathering tool 

*Step 1: Effect of EER 
Enforcement Respondent will be examined orally in Court or will make an affidavit on properties owned by him
O 22 r 11(1) 
- Enforcement Applicant may apply: 
* For Enforcement Respondent to be examined orally in Court or to make an affidavit on the properties owned by him => Whether beneficially in whole or in part or which the Enforcement Respondent will be entitled to in the future

Enforcement Respondent will be made to produce documents as are appropriate
O 22 r 11(2) 
- Enforcement Applicant may apply: 
* For Enforcement Respondent to produce documents as appropriate 

*Step 2: Application for EER
Enforcement Applicant may apply to Court for EER
O 22 r 11(1) 
- The enforcement applicant may apply for the enforcement respondent to be examined orally in court or to make an affidavit or both on the properties which are owned by the enforcement respondent beneficially whether in whole or in part or which the enforcement respondent will be entitled to in the future

Procedure to apply for EER 
Enforcement Applicant must make ex partes application to Court   
- Ex partes application for Court to grant order for EER 

In the application - Enforcement Applicant’s duty to provide full and frank disclosure 
The “Vasiliy Golovnin” 
- In the ex partes application: Applicant must disclose to the court all matters within his knowledge which might be material even if they are prejudicial to the applicant’s claim 

Court can grant leave to serve EER out of jurisdiction on a foreign officer of Enforcement Respondent (entity)
Test: Whether foreign officer was so closely connected with substantive claim that Singapore Court is justified in taking jurisdiction over foreign officer 
Burgundy Global Exploration Corp v Transocean Offshore International Ventures Ltd 
- Court’s discretion to grant leave to serve EER out of jurisdiction must be exercised sparingly 
- Test: Whether the foreign officer was so closely connected to the substantive claim that the Singapore Court is justified in taking jurisdiction over the foreign officer
a. Extent of foreign officer’s knowledge of enforcement respondent’s financial affairs
b. Extent of foreign officer’s involvement in matters relating to the claim 

*Step 3: After Court issues EER order, Enforcement Applicant must enforce EER by personally serving EER order on Enforcement Respondent  
Enforcement Applicant must personally serve EER Order (Form 41) on Enforcement Respondent
O 22 r 11(5)
- An order under this Rule must be in Form 41 and must be served personally on the enforcement respondent 

Enforcement Applicant must annex questionnaire (Form 41 or Form 42) to EER order for personal service 
Para 145 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- Questionnaire in the manner and form in Form 41 or 42 of Appendix B of PD must be annexed to order for examination of enforcement when the order is served on the enforcement respondent or its officers 
a. Form 41: For individual enforcement respondent 
b. Form 42: For officers of enforcement respondent entities 

Additional rules if Enforcement Respondent is an entity
If Enforcement Respondent is an entity => EER must state officers of entity who will be examined 
O 22 r 11(3)
- Where the enforcement respondent is an entity, the order must state the appointment of the officer or officers of the entity who are to be examined

If Enforcement Respondent is an entity => Form 41 must be personally served on any officer of entity who is ordered to attend examination hearing  
O 22 r 11(5)
- Where the enforcement respondent is an entity, Form 41 must be served personally on any officer of the entity ordered to attend for examination.

*Step 4A: If Enforcement Respondent completes questionnaire and serves completed questionnaire and supporting documents on Enforcement Applicant satisfactorily => Enforcement Applicant can request Enforcement Respondent provide their answers via affidavit or statutory declaration => Enforcement Applicant can apply to discharge EER Order => Hearing will not be held 
Para 145 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- Enforcement respondent need not attend at hearing if: 
a. He provides his answers to the questionnaire to the enforcement applicant by way of an affidavit or statutory declaration before the hearing 
b. The enforcement applicant agrees to apply for a discharge of the order for EER at the hearing 

*Step 4B: If Enforcement Respondent objects to questionnaire or refuses to comply satisfactorily => Enforcement Respondent must try to resolve issues with Enforcement Applicant before hearing => If not, parties have to go for examination hearing at the date and time in the EER Order 
Para 145 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- If enforcement respondent objects to any question in questionnaire on ground that it is unreasonable => Enforcement respondent must contact enforcement applicant to ascertain whether issue can be resolved prior to hearing 

*Step 5: At the examination hearing, Enforcement Applicant may examine Enforcement Respondent in relation to Enforcement Respondent’s assets => Enforcement Respondent needs to answer relevant questions under oath and produce supporting documents => Enforcement Applicant can request for Enforcement Respondent to file affidavit or statutory declaration => Enforcement Applicant can discharge EER Order 
Para 145 of Supreme Court Practice Directions 2021 
- At hearing, answered questionnaire is produced to Registrar and received as evidence upon the enforcement respondent’s confirmation on oath that his answers are true and correct => Enforcement applicant may then apply to discharge EER 


Enforcement of foreign judgements and arbitral awards 
Enforcement of Foreign Judgements 
Step 1: Judgement creditor must apply to register foreign judgement 
O 60 r 2(2)
- An application:
a. Foreign judgement from RECJA jurisdiction: Under section 3 of the first Act in respect of a judgment obtained in a superior court of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, or other territory to which section 5 of that Act applies; or
b. Foreign judgement from REFJA jurisdiction: Under section 4 of the second Act, in respect of a judgment to which that Act applies,
to have the judgment registered in the General Division must be made by originating application without notice.
=> Ex partes application by OA 

O 60 r 2(3)
- An application for registration must be supported by an affidavit:
a. Exhibiting the judgment or a verified or certified or otherwise duly authenticated copy of the judgment, and where the judgment is not in the English language, a translation of the judgment in that language certified by a notary public or authenticated by affidavit;
b. Stating the name, trade or business and the usual or last known place of residence or business of the judgment creditor and the judgment debtor respectively, so far as known to the deponent;
c. Stating to the best of the information or belief of the deponent:
(i) That the judgment creditor is entitled to enforce the judgment;
(ii) As the case may require, either that at the date of the application the judgment has not been satisfied, or the amount in respect of which it remains unsatisfied;
(iii) Where the application is made under the first Act, that the judgment does not fall within any of the cases in which a judgment may not be ordered to be registered under section 3(2) of that Act; and
(iv) Where the application is made under the second Act, that at the date of the application the judgment can be enforced by the issuance of an enforcement order in the country of the original court and that, if it were registered, the registration would not be, or be liable to be, set aside under section 5 of that Act; and
d. Specifying, where the application is made under the second Act, the amount of the interest (if any) which under the law of the country of the original court has become due under the judgment up to the time of registration.

Note: 
- O 60 r 4: Court may order judgement creditor to provide security for costs of application for registration and of any proceedings brought to set aside registration 

Step 2: If successful registration, obtain and serve Order of Registration on judgement debtor 
O 60 r 5
(1) Serve Order of Registration in Form 88 on judgement debtor: An order in Form 88 giving permission to register a judgment must be drawn up by, or on behalf of, the judgment creditor and served on the judgment debtor.
(2) Order of Registration must state period for judgement debtor to set aside registration: Every such order must state the period within which an application may be made to set aside the registration and must contain a notification that an enforcement order to enforce the judgment will not be issued until after the expiration of that period
(3) The Court may, on an application made at any time while it remains competent for any party to apply to have the registration set aside, extend the period (either as originally fixed or as subsequently extended) within which an application to have the registration set aside may be made.

Step 3: Serve Notice of Registration on judgement debtor + Endorsement of service 
O 60 r 7
(1) Serve Notice of Registration of judgement debtor: Notice of the registration of a judgment must be served on the judgment debtor and, subject to paragraph (2), must be served personally unless the Court otherwise orders.
(2) Service of such a notice out of Singapore is permissible without permission, and Order 8, Rules 2, 3, 7 and 8 apply in relation to such a notice as they apply in relation to an originating claim.
(3) Contents of Notice of Registration: The notice of registration must state:
a. Full particulars of the judgment registered and the order for registration;
b. The name and address of the judgment creditor or of the judgment creditor’s solicitor on whom, and at which, any summons issued by the judgment debtor may be served;
c. The right of the judgment debtor to apply to have the registration set aside; and
d. The period within which an application to set aside the registration may be made.

O 60 r 8
(1) Endorsement of service within 3 days after service: Within 3 days after service of the notice of registration or within such longer period as the Court may, in special circumstances, allow, the notice or a copy of the notice must be endorsed by the person who served it with the day of the week and date on which it was served; and, if the notice is not so endorsed within the abovementioned period, the judgment creditor may not apply for an enforcement order to enforce the judgment to which the notice relates without the permission of the Court.
(2) Every affidavit of service of any such notice must state the date on which the notice was endorsed under this Rule.

Step 4: Judgement debtor can make application to set aside registration 
O 60 r 9 
(1) Application to set aside registration by summons supported by affidavit: An application to set aside the registration of a judgment must be made by summons supported by an affidavit.
